Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

The National Forest Policy of 1988 aims to increase forest and tree cover to 33% of the country's geographical area.  Statement 1 accurately reflects this core objective.  Statement 3 is also correct; the policy actively promotes the use of wood substitutes and alternative fuel sources to lessen the dependence on forest resources for fuel and timber.  However, statement 2 is incorrect. While the policy acknowledges the importance of commercial forestry, it strongly cautions against monoculture plantations, recognizing their detrimental impact on biodiversity and ecological balance. The policy emphasizes the need for diverse and sustainable forest management practices.  The emphasis is on maintaining the ecological integrity of forests, not simply maximizing timber production through potentially damaging monoculture practices.



**2. With reference to the Kerala coast, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Kerala coast is characterized primarily by a coastline of submergence, resulting in extensive lagoons and backwaters.
2.  Monazite sands, a significant source of thorium, are found in substantial reserves along the Kerala coast.
3.  Indian shipping activity is heavily concentrated along the Kerala coast, making it a major hub for maritime trade.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 correctly identifies the presence of significant monazite sand reserves along the Kerala coast, a crucial source of thorium, a radioactive element with applications in nuclear energy and other industries. Statement 1 is incorrect; the Kerala coast is predominantly a coastline of emergence, formed by the uplift of the land, which has led to the formation of features like the backwaters and lagoons, but the process is not primarily submergence.  While the Kerala coast has some ports and participates in maritime activity, statement 3 exaggerates its role as a major hub for Indian shipping.  Other coastal regions of India, such as Mumbai and Chennai, have significantly larger and more established shipping industries. The Kerala coast's maritime activity is more localized and focused on smaller vessels and fishing.



**3. With reference to Ramsar sites in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Hokersar Wetland is a Ramsar site located in the state of Punjab.
2.  The Renuka Lake is a Ramsar site located in the state of Himachal Pradesh.
3.  The Sasthamkotta Lake is a Ramsar site located in the state of Tamil Nadu.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct; Renuka Lake is indeed a Ramsar site located in Himachal Pradesh.  Statements 1 and 3 are incorrect. The Hokersar Wetland is a Ramsar site located in Jammu and Kashmir, not Punjab. Sasthamkotta Lake is a Ramsar site located in Kerala, not Tamil Nadu.  These inaccuracies highlight the need for precise knowledge of the geographical locations of these significant wetlands. The question tests the candidate's ability to recall specific details regarding the location of Ramsar sites across different Indian states, demonstrating knowledge of India's conservation efforts.


**4. Consider the following statements about the National Chambal Sanctuary:**

1. The sanctuary supports a viable population of the Gharial (Gavialis gangeticus).
2. The sanctuary is located entirely within the state of Madhya Pradesh.
3. The sanctuary primarily protects a diverse range of  tropical moist deciduous forest ecosystems.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct; the National Chambal Sanctuary is known for its significant gharial population.  Statement 2 is incorrect, as the sanctuary actually extends across three states: Madhya Pradesh, Rajasthan, and Uttar Pradesh. Statement 3 is also incorrect; the sanctuary's ecosystem is predominantly characterized by the riverine habitat of the Chambal River, not tropical moist deciduous forests. The sanctuary's importance lies in its conservation of the gharial and other endangered species adapted to the specific conditions of the Chambal river system. The question tests the candidate's knowledge of the geographical extent and ecological characteristics of a crucial wildlife sanctuary in India.


**5. With reference to butterflies and their distribution, consider the following statements:**

1. The majority of butterfly species are found in temperate regions due to the abundance of flowering plants.
2. Butterflies have a high tolerance for extreme temperatures, allowing them to thrive in diverse climates.
3.  Low temperatures significantly limit butterfly distribution, with tropical regions showing greater diversity.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a) 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 3 accurately reflects the relationship between temperature and butterfly distribution. Butterflies are ectothermic, meaning their body temperature is dependent on the environment. Low temperatures restrict their activity and survival, leading to greater species diversity in warmer, tropical climates.  Statements 1 and 2 are incorrect. Temperate regions, while having flowering plants, do not support the same level of butterfly diversity as tropical regions. Butterflies also have limited temperature tolerance; extreme temperatures, both high and low, can negatively affect their survival and reproduction.  The question tests the candidate's understanding of ecological factors influencing biodiversity and species distribution.  The distractors emphasize common misconceptions about butterfly biology and distribution.


These questions are designed to be challenging, requiring detailed knowledge of the topics.  The distractors are carefully chosen to be plausible, testing the candidate's ability to differentiate between closely related concepts.

**1. Consider the following statements:**

1. Project Tiger, launched in 1973, initially focused on conserving tiger populations within Jim Corbett National Park and was centrally sponsored by the Ministry of Environment and Forests (MoEF).
2.  The National Tiger Conservation Authority (NTCA) administers Project Tiger and conducts the Tiger Census, a four-yearly survey utilizing camera trapping and DNA fingerprinting techniques to monitor tiger populations.
3. Project Tiger's success is solely attributable to the relocation of villages from tiger reserves, providing financial aid of ₹10 lakh per family for relocation.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct. Project Tiger was indeed launched in 1973, focusing initially on Jim Corbett National Park.  The MoEF played a crucial role in its central sponsorship. However, the statement incorrectly implies that the initial focus was *solely* on Jim Corbett.  Project Tiger expanded rapidly to encompass other tiger reserves across India.

Statement 2 is correct. The NTCA is the key administrative body for Project Tiger and is responsible for the Tiger Census. While pugmark analysis was historically used, the statement accurately reflects the current reliance on camera trapping and DNA fingerprinting for more accurate population estimations.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While village relocation from critical tiger habitats played a role in reducing human-wildlife conflict and improving tiger conservation, it was not the *sole* factor contributing to Project Tiger's success.  Other crucial factors include improved anti-poaching measures, habitat restoration, and increased community participation in conservation efforts.  Attributing success solely to relocation is an oversimplification and a misleading statement. The financial aid amount mentioned might also be an approximation or specific to a certain period.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are partially or fully correct.


**2. Consider the following statements:**

1. The first National Centre for Marine Biodiversity (NCMB) in India is located in Mumbai, a city known for its significant Zoroastrian population and historical development by the British.
2.  Jamnagar, a defence town in Gujarat, houses India's only NCMB and is also home to the Nageshvara Jyotirlinga temple.
3. Bhavnagar, another city in Gujarat, is renowned for its significant seaweed resources and is not associated with any NCMB.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The provided text states that India's first National Centre for Marine Biodiversity is located in Bhavnagar, not Mumbai.  While Mumbai is a major coastal city with a significant Zoroastrian population and a history of British development, it does not house the first NCMB.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Jamnagar is mentioned in the text, but not in relation to an NCMB.  The information provided about it (defence town, Nageshvara Jyotirlinga) is accurate.  However, linking it to the NCMB is a false connection.

Statement 3 is correct. The text explicitly mentions Bhavnagar in Gujarat and its association with significant seaweed resources. It is correctly stated that Bhavnagar is not associated with the NCMB.

Therefore, only statement 3 is correct.


**3. With reference to in-situ conservation strategies, consider the following statements:**

1.  Botanical gardens, while involved in conservation, are examples of ex-situ conservation, not in-situ conservation because they involve the removal of species from their natural habitats.
2.  Biosphere reserves and national parks are examples of in-situ conservation, as they protect species within their natural habitats.
3. Sacred groves, traditional protected areas managed by local communities, are not considered a form of in-situ conservation due to lack of formal governmental recognition.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Botanical gardens are a prime example of ex-situ conservation.  Plants are cultivated outside their natural environment, often for research, display, or propagation purposes. This contrasts with in-situ conservation, which focuses on preserving species within their natural habitats.

Statement 2 is correct. Biosphere reserves and national parks are explicitly designed for in-situ conservation.  They establish protected areas where species continue to live in their natural ecosystems, with minimal human interference.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  Sacred groves are indeed traditionally managed protected areas but are absolutely considered  a form of in-situ conservation. Although they may lack formal governmental recognition in some cases, their crucial role in preserving biodiversity within the natural environment makes them a vital part of in-situ conservation strategies.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are correct.


**4. With reference to Dachigam National Park, consider the following statements:**

1. Dachigam National Park, located in the Zabarwan Range of Jammu and Kashmir, is primarily associated with the conservation of the Hangul (Kashmir stag), an endangered species.
2.  The park also provides habitat for musk deer, but its primary conservation focus is the Golden Oriole.
3. The Yellow-throated Marten, while present in the Himalayan region, is not a primary focus of conservation efforts within Dachigam National Park.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Dachigam National Park's main conservation objective is the protection of the Hangul (Kashmir stag), a critically endangered subspecies unique to the region.  Its location in the Zabarwan Range of Jammu and Kashmir is also accurate.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While musk deer are present in Dachigam,  the park's primary focus is not on the Golden Oriole. The focus is on the Hangul.  The statement wrongly assigns the primary conservation focus.

Statement 3 is correct. The Yellow-throated Marten has a wider distribution than just Dachigam, and while it might inhabit the park, it is not the park's primary conservation concern.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are correct.


**5. Consider the following statements about animals and their water requirements:**

1. Camels can survive for extended periods without drinking water due to their efficient metabolic processes and ability to tolerate high levels of dehydration.
2.  Kangaroo rats are known for their exceptional ability to survive without drinking water, extracting moisture from their food.
3. Giraffes require frequent water intake due to their large size and high metabolic rate, making them less tolerant to dehydration than camels or kangaroo rats.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Camels are renowned for their ability to endure long periods without water, thanks to adaptations such as efficient water metabolism and the capacity to tolerate significant water loss.

Statement 2 is correct. Kangaroo rats are desert-dwelling rodents with remarkable adaptations to arid conditions. They obtain most of their water requirements from the metabolic breakdown of food, reducing their need for direct water intake.

Statement 3 is correct. Giraffes, despite their access to water sources in their habitat, have a high metabolic rate due to their size, requiring relatively frequent water consumption.  They are less adapted to water scarcity than desert-dwelling animals.

Therefore, all three statements are correct.


**6. Consider the following statements regarding ecosystems and plant biomass:**

1. Temperate deciduous forests exhibit higher plant biomass compared to tropical deciduous forests due to longer growing seasons and less intense competition among species.
2. Tropical rainforests, characterized by high rainfall and species diversity, typically have the highest plant biomass among all terrestrial ecosystems.
3. Desert shrublands, with their limited water availability and sparse vegetation, naturally possess the lowest plant biomass among the given options.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While temperate deciduous forests have a significant biomass, tropical rainforests generally surpass them due to their consistently warm temperatures, high rainfall, and the resulting lush, multi-layered vegetation.  The statement incorrectly compares the biomass of these two forest types.

Statement 2 is correct. Tropical rainforests are known for their exceptionally high plant biomass, a result of optimal growing conditions and the high density of vegetation.

Statement 3 is correct. Desert shrublands are characterized by water scarcity and limited plant growth, resulting in the lowest plant biomass among the given options.

Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are correct.


**7.  Consider the following statements regarding the location of National Parks in India:**

1.  Bandipur National Park is located in Uttarakhand, known for its diverse flora and fauna, including the tiger.
2. Rajaji National Park is situated in Odisha, famous for its Similipal Biosphere Reserve and diverse tribal cultures.
3. Similipal National Park is found in Karnataka, a state known for its rich biodiversity and coffee plantations.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Bandipur National Park is actually located in Karnataka, not Uttarakhand.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Rajaji National Park is located in Uttarakhand, not Odisha.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Similipal National Park is situated in Odisha, not Karnataka.

Therefore, none of the statements are correct.  The question highlights the importance of accurate geographical knowledge of Indian National Parks for UPSC aspirants.


**8. Consider the following statements about protected mangrove regions in India:**

1. The Eastern Ghats, a mountain range in eastern India, features extensive mangrove forests along its coast.
2.  The Western Ghats, while known for its rich biodiversity, predominantly comprises rainforest and doesn't have significant mangrove cover.
3.  Goa's coastline includes protected mangrove areas, but their extent is relatively small compared to the Sundarbans.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  Mangrove forests are primarily associated with coastal areas, and while the Eastern Ghats are near the coast, they are not predominantly mangrove habitat.  The statement incorrectly associates mangroves with the Eastern Ghats.

Statement 2 is correct. The Western Ghats are known for their unique biodiversity, but they are not significantly characterized by mangrove ecosystems.  The dominant vegetation there is rainforest.

Statement 3 is partially correct. Goa does have some mangrove areas, but these are smaller and less extensive than the vast mangrove forests of the Sundarbans.  The statement accurately points out the relatively limited scale of Goa's mangrove cover.

Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are correct.


**9. Consider the following statements about Suklaphanta Wildlife Reserve:**

1. Suklaphanta Wildlife Reserve is located in Bhutan, known for its unique biodiversity and Gross National Happiness (GNH) index.
2.  This reserve is situated in Myanmar, a country with a diverse range of ecosystems and a history of opium production.
3.  Suklaphanta Wildlife Reserve is located in Nepal, and is known for its significant population of the Indian rhinoceros.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Suklaphanta Wildlife Reserve is not in Bhutan. Bhutan is known for its GNH index and unique biodiversity, but this specific reserve is not located there.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Suklaphanta Wildlife Reserve is not situated in Myanmar. Myanmar has a diverse range of ecosystems and a historical association with opium production, but this reserve is not located within its borders.

Statement 3 is correct. The text accurately places Suklaphanta Wildlife Reserve in Nepal.  The statement about the Indian rhinoceros is incorrect, however, as the text does not mention the presence of rhinoceros in this reserve.


Therefore, only statement 3 is partially correct.


**10. Consider the following statements:**

1. The most significant aspect of biodiversity is its contribution to food security, encompassing a wide range of crops and livestock.
2.  Biodiversity's role in pharmaceutical development is significant, with numerous medicines derived from natural sources.
3.  The industrial use of biodiversity is less significant than its roles in food and drug production, as most industries do not rely on natural resources.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Biodiversity underpins food security by providing a vast array of crops, livestock, and other food sources. The diversity of these resources is crucial for resilience against pests, diseases, and climate change.

Statement 2 is correct. A significant portion of modern pharmaceuticals are derived from, or inspired by, natural sources. Biodiversity provides a vast library of potential drug compounds.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The industrial use of biodiversity is substantial, encompassing materials like timber, fibers, resins, and many other resources.  Many industries heavily rely on natural products.


Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are correct.


**11. Consider the following statements about biodiversity-saturated areas in India:**

1. The Eastern Ghats, while possessing some biodiversity, are less saturated compared to the Western Ghats.
2. The Western Ghats are a biodiversity hotspot with high levels of endemism and species richness.
3. The Thar Desert, due to its arid conditions, has low biodiversity and is not considered a biodiversity-saturated area.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2 and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Western Ghats are recognized as a global biodiversity hotspot, exhibiting significantly higher levels of endemism and species richness than the Eastern Ghats.

Statement 2 is correct. The Western Ghats are indeed a globally recognized biodiversity hotspot, characterized by high levels of endemism (species found nowhere else) and exceptional species richness.

Statement 3 is correct.  The Thar Desert's arid conditions limit biodiversity, resulting in a much lower species richness and endemism compared to the Western Ghats.

Therefore, all three statements are correct.


**12. Consider the following statements about factors affecting biodiversity in an ecosystem:**

1. High ecosystem productivity generally leads to increased biodiversity, providing more resources and supporting a wider range of species.
2. Intermediate levels of disturbance can enhance biodiversity by preventing competitive exclusion and creating ecological niches for diverse species.
3.  A younger ecosystem, with less time for species to evolve and diversify, typically exhibits lower biodiversity than an older, more established ecosystem.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Higher productivity in an ecosystem generally translates to greater resource availability, supporting a larger number of individuals and a wider variety of species.

Statement 2 is correct.  The intermediate disturbance hypothesis proposes that moderate levels of disturbance prevent any single species from dominating the ecosystem, creating opportunities for various species to coexist.  Extreme disturbances, on the other hand, can reduce biodiversity.

Statement 3 is correct.  Ecosystems take time to develop biodiversity. Younger ecosystems haven't had sufficient time for species to colonize, adapt, and diversify to the extent seen in mature ecosystems.

Therefore, all three statements are correct.  This question tests understanding of ecological principles related to biodiversity.


**13. Consider the following statements regarding coral bleaching:**

1.  Global warming, leading to increased sea temperatures, is the primary driver of coral bleaching, stressing coral polyps and causing them to expel their symbiotic algae.
2. While coral diseases can contribute to coral mortality, they are not the most significant factor in widespread coral bleaching events.
3. Siltation of seawater, reducing water clarity and light penetration, is a major cause of widespread coral bleaching events.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Global warming and the resulting rise in sea surface temperatures are the main cause of large-scale coral bleaching events.  Elevated temperatures stress the symbiotic algae (zooxanthellae) living within coral polyps, causing the corals to expel the algae, leading to bleaching.

Statement 2 is correct. Coral diseases can certainly harm coral reefs, but they are not the primary factor behind widespread coral bleaching.  Bleaching is primarily a temperature-driven phenomenon.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While siltation can negatively impact coral reefs by reducing light penetration and causing smothering, it is not the main factor in widespread coral bleaching.  The primary cause remains elevated sea temperatures due to global warming.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are correct.  This question tests understanding of the environmental impact of global warming on marine ecosystems.


**14. Consider the following statements about marine national parks in India:**

1.  The Gulf of Mannar Marine National Park is located off the coast of Tamil Nadu and is known for its rich biodiversity, including dugongs and sea turtles.
2.  The Mahatma Gandhi Marine National Park is located in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands and protects a variety of marine species.
3.  The Lakshadweep Marine National Park is not a protected area designated as a marine national park in India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Gulf of Mannar Marine National Park is indeed located off the coast of Tamil Nadu and is well-known for its diverse marine life, including dugongs and various species of sea turtles.

Statement 2 is correct.  The Mahatma Gandhi Marine National Park in the Andaman and Nicobar Islands is a recognized marine national park protecting a wide array of marine flora and fauna.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Lakshadweep Marine National Park is a designated protected area in India.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are correct.  The question assesses knowledge of specific marine protected areas in India.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding coral reefs:**

1.  Coral diseases, such as white band disease, primarily affect the coral polyp, leading to its death and subsequent colony collapse.
2.  Eutrophication, characterized by excessive nutrient enrichment in seawater, significantly increases the susceptibility of coral to diseases.
3.  The Kyoto Protocol directly addresses the mitigation of coral reef bleaching caused by global warming.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Coral diseases directly impact the coral polyp, the living animal forming the coral structure.  The death of polyps leads to the degradation and eventual death of the entire coral colony.  Various diseases, such as white band disease, black band disease, and white pox, cause significant coral mortality.

Statement 2 is also correct. Eutrophication, stemming from increased nutrient runoff (nitrogen and phosphorus), fuels algal blooms. These blooms can smother corals, reduce light penetration necessary for photosynthesis by symbiotic zooxanthellae (algae living within corals), and weaken the coral's immune system, making them more vulnerable to diseases.  This creates a synergistic effect where eutrophication and disease work together to cause extensive damage.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Kyoto Protocol aims to reduce greenhouse gas emissions, a major driver of global warming and consequently coral bleaching, it doesn't directly address coral reef bleaching as a specific target.  The protocol focuses on broader climate change mitigation strategies.  Addressing coral bleaching requires specific localized conservation and management efforts in addition to global climate action.



**2. With reference to the impacts of global warming, consider the following statements:**

1.  Global warming, a component of climate change, necessitates governmental action to mitigate its adverse effects on surge-type glaciers.
2.  The thawing of permafrost and wildfires are direct causes of global warming, initiating a positive feedback loop that accelerates the warming process.
3.  The injection of sulphate aerosol into the stratosphere is a climate engineering technique proposed to directly mitigate global warming by reflecting solar radiation.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While global warming does indeed affect surge-type glaciers, causing instability and potential catastrophic events, the statement oversimplifies the relationship.  Governmental action is crucial, but it’s not solely focused on surge-type glaciers;  it encompasses a much broader range of climate change adaptation and mitigation strategies related to various environmental impacts.

Statement 2 is correct. Thawing permafrost releases large amounts of methane, a potent greenhouse gas, into the atmosphere, which further accelerates global warming. Wildfires also release significant amounts of carbon dioxide and other greenhouse gases, contributing to the warming trend.  This creates a positive feedback loop, where warming triggers events that further enhance warming.

Statement 3 is correct. Stratospheric aerosol injection is a proposed geoengineering technique to cool the planet by reflecting a portion of incoming solar radiation back into space.  It directly addresses global warming by attempting to reduce the amount of solar energy absorbed by the Earth's surface and atmosphere.  However, the long-term effects and potential risks associated with this technique are still under intense debate and research.



**3.  Consider the following statements about the Gulf of Mannar:**

1.  The Gulf of Mannar, located near India, is adjacent to the Palk Strait and contains extensive seagrass beds that serve as a habitat for dugongs.
2.  The Gulf of Mannar Marine National Park is primarily known for its diverse coral reefs, which are threatened by global warming and coral diseases.
3.  The Chidambaram Port, located within the Gulf of Mannar, significantly contributes to the region's economic activity and has minimal environmental impact.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Gulf of Mannar is indeed located near India, adjacent to the Palk Strait.  Its seagrass meadows provide crucial habitat for dugongs (sea cows), an endangered marine mammal.  The presence of seagrass is a key indicator of a healthy marine ecosystem.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Gulf of Mannar Marine National Park is renowned for its rich biodiversity, including coral reefs.  However, these reefs, like many others globally, face significant threats from global warming (causing coral bleaching) and coral diseases.  This highlights the vulnerability of these ecosystems to both global and local environmental stressors.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Chidambaram Port contributes to economic activity, its impact on the environment is not minimal.  Port activities, including shipping traffic, dredging, and potential pollution from waste disposal, can negatively affect the delicate marine ecosystem of the Gulf of Mannar.  Sustainable port management is crucial to minimize these negative impacts.


**4. With reference to Bhutan's environmental policies, consider the following statements:**

1. Bhutan, a country located in the Eastern Himalayas, shares a border with India and has achieved carbon neutrality.
2.  The Royal Manas National Park in Bhutan, contiguous with Manas National Park in India, is a significant biodiversity hotspot known for its population of Wild Water Buffalo.
3.  Bhutan's Gross National Happiness (GNH) index incorporates environmental sustainability as a key indicator.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Bhutan, situated in the Eastern Himalayas, shares a border with India.  A notable achievement of Bhutan is its commitment to and attainment of carbon neutrality, demonstrating a strong focus on environmental protection.

Statement 2 is correct. The Royal Manas National Park in Bhutan is indeed contiguous with Manas National Park in India, forming a significant transboundary protected area.  Both parks are known for their rich biodiversity, including populations of endangered species like the Wild Water Buffalo. The connectivity of these parks is crucial for wildlife conservation.

Statement 3 is correct. Bhutan's Gross National Happiness (GNH) index is a unique development philosophy that prioritizes societal well-being, including environmental sustainability.  The GNH index goes beyond traditional economic indicators like GDP to encompass factors like environmental conservation, health, and education, reflecting a holistic approach to development.


**5. Consider the following statements regarding Australia's environment and economy:**

1. Australia, the driest inhabited continent, experiences frequent bushfires exacerbated by global warming, resulting in significant biodiversity loss, including koala deaths.
2. Australia is a major exporter of coal, contributing significantly to global carbon emissions, while simultaneously employing carbon credit mechanisms as part of its environmental policy.
3. The Great Barrier Reef, located off the coast of Australia, is a UNESCO World Heritage Site and is highly threatened by ocean acidification, a process analogous to global warming.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Australia's arid climate and susceptibility to bushfires are well documented. Global warming intensifies these fires, leading to extensive habitat loss and impacting wildlife populations, including koalas. This highlights the interconnectedness of climate change and biodiversity loss.

Statement 2 is correct. Australia is a significant coal producer and exporter, a major contributor to global greenhouse gas emissions.  The country also implements carbon credit schemes as part of its climate change mitigation strategy. This demonstrates the complex interplay between economic interests and environmental concerns.

Statement 3 is correct. The Great Barrier Reef is a globally recognized natural wonder and a UNESCO World Heritage Site. Ocean acidification, caused by increased absorption of carbon dioxide by the oceans, is a serious threat to coral reefs, making it analogous to global warming's impact through coral bleaching.  Both processes lead to the degradation of this vital ecosystem.


**6. With reference to India's biodiversity hotspots, consider the following statements:**

1. The Eastern Himalayas biodiversity hotspot includes parts of Bhutan, Nepal, China, and Myanmar, in addition to India's northeastern region.
2. The Indo-Burma hotspot is threatened by industrial forestry, particularly palm and rubber plantations, driving species extinction.
3. The Western Ghats and Sri Lanka hotspot is characterized by high levels of endemism in amphibians and reptiles.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Eastern Himalayas biodiversity hotspot is a transboundary region encompassing parts of several countries including Bhutan, Nepal, China, and Myanmar, in addition to the northeastern states of India.  The region is known for its rich biodiversity and high levels of endemism.

Statement 2 is correct. The Indo-Burma hotspot faces significant threats from large-scale industrial forestry, particularly the expansion of palm oil and rubber plantations.  These activities lead to widespread deforestation and habitat fragmentation, placing numerous species at risk of extinction.

Statement 3 is correct. The Western Ghats and Sri Lanka hotspot exhibits remarkably high levels of endemism, particularly among amphibians and reptiles.  This high endemism highlights the unique evolutionary history and ecological significance of this region, emphasizing the need for focused conservation efforts.


**7. Consider the following statements regarding the Montreux Record:**

1.  A wetland's inclusion in the Montreux Record signifies that ecological changes are occurring due to human interference, necessitating remedial action.
2. The Montreux Record designation automatically grants the wetland World Heritage Site status.
3. Wetlands included in the Montreux Record are subject to stricter regulations regarding human activities within a specified radius of the wetland boundary.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Montreux Record, maintained under the Ramsar Convention, identifies wetlands where ecological character has changed, is changing, or is likely to change as a result of human impacts.  This designation signals the need for conservation and restoration efforts to address the identified problems.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The Montreux Record and the World Heritage Site designation are distinct. While both relate to conservation, they have different criteria and implications.  World Heritage Site status is a broader recognition of cultural or natural significance, while the Montreux Record specifically targets ecological changes in wetlands.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While the Montreux Record highlights the need for action, it doesn't automatically impose stricter regulations within a set radius of the wetland.  The specific management strategies and regulations implemented will vary depending on the individual wetland and the country's policies.  The Ramsar convention encourages but doesn't mandate specific actions.


**8. With reference to India's Biosphere Reserves, consider the following statements:**

1. The Agasthyamala Biosphere Reserve includes Neyyar, Peppara, and Shendurney wildlife sanctuaries, and the Kalakad Mundanthurai Tiger Reserve.
2. The Great Nicobar Biosphere Reserve comprises Campbell Bay and Galathea National Parks and is characterized by tropical wet evergreen forests.
3. The Manas Biosphere Reserve, located partially in Bhutan, is known for its population of Wild Water Buffalo and is a UNESCO World Heritage Site.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Agasthyamala Biosphere Reserve includes the mentioned wildlife sanctuaries and tiger reserve, demonstrating the interconnectedness of protected areas in this region.  This highlights the importance of integrated conservation strategies.

Statement 2 is correct. The Great Nicobar Biosphere Reserve is correctly described as encompassing both Campbell Bay and Galathea National Parks, characterized by tropical wet evergreen forests. This unique ecosystem supports a range of endemic flora and fauna.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Manas Biosphere Reserve does share a border with Bhutan and is known for its Wild Water Buffalo, it's not a UNESCO World Heritage Site, although the Manas Wildlife Sanctuary *within* the biosphere reserve is.  The distinction is key, highlighting the importance of carefully understanding the designations of protected areas.


**9. Consider the following statements about Biodiversity Heritage Sites (BHS) in India:**

1. The designation of an area as a BHS automatically restricts the prevailing practices and usages of local communities within that area.
2. Majuli, the world's largest river island in Assam, is recognized as a BHS for its unique biodiversity and neo-Vaishnavite monasteries.
3.  The Hajong Tortoise Lake in Assam, a BHS, is a critical habitat for endangered freshwater turtles, including the Indian Peacock Softshell Turtle.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The declaration of a Biodiversity Heritage Site (BHS) under Section 37 of the Biological Diversity Act, 2002, does *not* automatically restrict the prevailing practices and usages of the local communities. The aim is to enhance the quality of life of local communities *through* conservation.  This demonstrates a community-centric approach to conservation.

Statement 2 is correct. Majuli Island in Assam is indeed the world's largest river island and is designated as a BHS due to its rich biodiversity and cultural significance, including its neo-Vaishnavite monasteries and traditional way of life.  This shows the integration of cultural and biological conservation.

Statement 3 is correct. Hajong Tortoise Lake is a BHS and is indeed an important habitat for endangered freshwater turtles, including the Indian Peacock Softshell Turtle.  This highlights the significance of BHS in protecting specific threatened species and their habitats.



**10. With reference to ecological succession, consider the following statements:**

1. In primary succession, lichens and mosses act as pioneer species, colonizing areas like rock outcrops and glacial moraines.
2. Secondary succession occurs faster than primary succession because it starts on existing soil, leading to a quicker establishment of a climax community.
3. In grasslands, trees typically replace grasses as part of ecological succession due to the gradual increase in soil nutrients and available sunlight.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Lichens and mosses are indeed pioneer species in primary succession, capable of colonizing bare rock surfaces and other substrates lacking pre-existing soil.  They initiate soil formation through their decomposition, creating conditions suitable for more complex plant life.

Statement 2 is correct. Secondary succession is generally faster than primary succession because it begins with pre-existing soil and often retains some elements of the previous community.  This established base allows for quicker colonization and establishment of a climax community.

Statement 3 is incorrect. In grasslands, trees do *not* typically replace grasses in ecological succession.  Factors like limited water availability, fire frequency, and nutrient cycling often prevent tree establishment, maintaining the grassland ecosystem as a stable climax community.  This illustrates the influence of abiotic factors on ecological succession.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, focusing on Madhya Pradesh, Uttar Pradesh, Andhra Pradesh, Karnataka, Gujarat, and West Bengal.  Each question adheres to the specified criteria, including difficulty level and distractor design.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding Madhya Pradesh's geography and resources:**

1.  Madhya Pradesh's extensive forest cover, exceeding 30% of its geographical area, is primarily composed of the Vindhyas mountain range.
2.  The Chambal and Son rivers, significant tributaries of the Ganga-Yamuna doab, define the northern and eastern boundaries of Madhya Pradesh.
3.  Madhya Pradesh is a leading producer of copper ore, while its dolomite reserves are among the largest in India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct.  Madhya Pradesh has a significant forest cover, but the statement exaggerates the proportion and the dominant geographical feature. While the Vindhyas are a significant part of the state's landscape, they do not constitute the majority of its forest cover.  The Satpura range also plays a crucial role.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Chambal and Son rivers are indeed important rivers in Madhya Pradesh, but they are not tributaries of the Ganga-Yamuna *doab* (a region).  The doab is an interfluvial area *between* the Ganga and Yamuna. The Chambal flows into the Yamuna, and the Son flows into the Ganga, but neither defines the boundary of Madhya Pradesh in relation to the doab.

Statement 3 is correct. Madhya Pradesh is indeed a major producer of copper ore, and its dolomite reserves are substantial. This makes option (b) the most appropriate answer.


**2. With reference to the socio-economic characteristics of Uttar Pradesh, consider the following statements:**

1.  Uttar Pradesh's high population density is primarily attributed to its extensive alluvial deposits, leading to fertile agricultural land and high agricultural labor concentration.
2.  The state's high proportion of agricultural laborers contributes significantly to its low urbanization rate, despite its significant industrial output.
3.  Uttar Pradesh, a major producer of rapeseed and mustard, has experienced a consistent growth rate of 20-25 percent during the period 2001-2011.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct. Uttar Pradesh's high population density is linked to its fertile alluvial plains, supporting a large agricultural population. This leads to a high concentration of agricultural laborers.

Statement 2 is correct. The dependence on agriculture and the large number of agricultural labourers do contribute to a lower urbanization rate compared to other states with more diversified economies, despite industrial growth in certain areas.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While Uttar Pradesh is a significant producer of rapeseed and mustard and did experience growth during 2001-2011, a consistent 20-25% annual growth rate is an overstatement.  Growth rates fluctuate and vary across sectors.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are entirely accurate.


**3. With reference to Andhra Pradesh's economy and resources, consider the following statements:**

1.  Andhra Pradesh, a major producer of groundnut and chillies, experienced a significant increase in forest cover by 647 sq km between 2001 and 2011.
2.  The state's coastal location and the Godavari-Krishna delta region contribute significantly to its agricultural output, particularly in rice and cotton production.
3.  Andhra Pradesh holds substantial reserves of dolomite and has liberalized its land leasing laws, facilitating increased agricultural productivity.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Andhra Pradesh is a significant producer of groundnut and chillies, the 647 sq km increase in forest cover is linked to a different state.  The figure needs to be verified for Andhra Pradesh.

Statement 2 is correct.  Andhra Pradesh's coastal location and fertile delta regions are crucial for its agriculture, particularly rice and cotton.

Statement 3 is partially correct. Andhra Pradesh has substantial dolomite reserves. However, the characterization of its land leasing laws as "liberalized" requires further clarification. The laws have undergone changes but might not be as liberal as implied.   Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are sufficiently accurate.


**4. With reference to Karnataka's cultural heritage and industries, consider the following statements:**

1.  Karnataka's "vesara" architectural style, evident in numerous temples, is influenced by the region's proximity to the Western Ghats and its rich Jain traditions.
2.  The state's sandalwood industry, known for its high-quality output, is concentrated primarily in the coastal regions and its production is largely driven by high FDI.
3.  The Bidri craft, a unique metal inlay technique, originated in Karnataka, and the state is also renowned for its production of Jain bronzes.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The vesara style is indeed characteristic of Karnataka temple architecture, reflecting local influences and religious practices.

Statement 2 is partially incorrect. While Karnataka is famous for its sandalwood industry, the concentration is not limited to coastal regions and FDI is not the primary driver of its production.  The industry is more closely tied to traditional practices and local resources.

Statement 3 is correct.  Bidriware is a significant craft of Karnataka and the state is indeed known for its Jain bronzes.  This makes option (a) the most suitable choice.


**5. Consider the following statements about Gujarat's geography and resources:**

1.  Gujarat's extensive coastline, bordering the Arabian Sea, contributes significantly to its crude oil and natural gas production, making it a major energy producer in India.
2.  The state's arid climate and the Thar Desert region influence its agricultural practices, with significant dependence on irrigation for crops like cotton and groundnut.
3.  Gujarat's mangrove cover, among the largest in India, is concentrated in the Gulf of Kutch and Kori Creek regions, playing a crucial role in biodiversity conservation.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Gujarat's coastal location and offshore resources do contribute substantially to its oil and gas production.

Statement 2 is correct.  The arid climate necessitates irrigation for successful agriculture in Gujarat. Cotton and groundnut are important crops in the state.

Statement 3 is correct. Gujarat possesses a significant mangrove cover, much of which is located in the Gulf of Kutch and Kori Creek.  Therefore, all three statements are factually accurate.


**6. With reference to West Bengal's economy and environment, consider the following statements:**

1.  West Bengal, a major producer of jute and rice, has a high population density concentrated in its deltaic regions, leading to a high proportion of agricultural laborers.
2.  The state's extensive mangrove forests in the Sundarbans, a UNESCO World Heritage Site, are threatened by cyclones and coastal erosion, impacting biodiversity.
3.  West Bengal's forest cover, which includes significant areas under the Eastern Himalayas, has experienced a consistent increase in recent years, primarily due to successful reforestation efforts.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct. Jute and rice are important crops in West Bengal, and the high population density in the deltaic regions does contribute to a large agricultural workforce.

Statement 2 is correct. The Sundarbans mangroves are indeed a World Heritage site and face threats from cyclones and erosion.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While West Bengal has significant forest cover in the Eastern Himalayas, a consistent increase in recent years needs further verification. The statement oversimplifies a complex situation where deforestation and other challenges exist alongside conservation initiatives.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 2 are fully supported by factual evidence.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Note that the difficulty level is subjective and depends on the examinee's prior knowledge.  These questions are designed to be challenging, requiring in-depth understanding and recall of specific details.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Great Indian Bustard:**

1.  The Great Indian Bustard is classified as Critically Endangered (CR) by the International Union for Conservation of Nature (IUCN).
2.  Significant populations of the Great Indian Bustard are found within the boundaries of the Keoladeo Ghana National Park in Rajasthan.
3.  The species is listed under Appendix II of the Convention on the Conservation of Migratory Species of Wild Animals (CMS).

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The IUCN Red List indeed categorizes the Great Indian Bustard as Critically Endangered, reflecting its extremely high risk of extinction in the wild.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Great Indian Bustard's habitat overlaps with areas near Keoladeo Ghana National Park, significant populations are not *within* its boundaries. The bird prefers grasslands and open scrublands, unlike the more forested areas of Keoladeo Ghana.  Key habitats for the Great Indian Bustard are found in other protected areas like Desert National Park (Rajasthan), Kutch Bustard Sanctuary (Gujarat), and others mentioned in the source material.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Great Indian Bustard is listed under Appendix I of CMS, not Appendix II. Appendix I lists species that are threatened with extinction, requiring stricter conservation measures.  Appendix II includes species that require international cooperation to ensure their conservation, but the level of threat is not as severe as for Appendix I.  The distinction is crucial for understanding the conservation priorities and the level of protection afforded to the species.


**2. With reference to the conservation efforts for the Great Indian Bustard, consider the following statements:**

1.  The species is protected under Schedule I of the Wildlife Protection Act of India (WPA).
2.  The Rollapadu Wildlife Sanctuary plays a significant role in the conservation of the Great Indian Bustard.
3.  The establishment of the Karera Wildlife Sanctuary was primarily aimed at protecting the habitat of the Great Indian Bustard.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Great Indian Bustard enjoys the highest level of protection afforded by the WPA under Schedule I, highlighting its critical conservation status.

Statement 2 is correct. The Rollapadu Wildlife Sanctuary in Andhra Pradesh is one of the crucial habitats and breeding grounds for the Great Indian Bustard, contributing significantly to its conservation.

Statement 3 is correct. The Karera Wildlife Sanctuary in Madhya Pradesh was indeed established with the primary goal of safeguarding the dwindling population of the Great Indian Bustard and its habitat.  The sanctuary's establishment demonstrates a targeted conservation strategy for this critically endangered species.


**3.  With reference to the geographical distribution of the Great Indian Bustard, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Great Indian Bustard is primarily found in the high-altitude regions of the Himalayas.
2.  The species' range extends to the Great Rann of Kutch Biosphere Reserve.
3.  The Ghatigaon Wildlife Sanctuary provides a significant habitat for the Great Indian Bustard.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Great Indian Bustard inhabits arid and semi-arid grasslands and scrublands in the plains of India, not the high-altitude Himalayan regions.  The Himalayan region has a different set of avian and mammalian species adapted to high-altitude conditions.

Statement 2 is correct.  The Great Rann of Kutch Biosphere Reserve, known for its unique ecosystem, includes habitats suitable for the Great Indian Bustard, contributing to its overall distribution.

Statement 3 is correct.  The Ghatigaon Wildlife Sanctuary provides a habitat for the Great Indian Bustard, which is crucial for its survival and conservation.


**4. Consider the following statements about the conservation status of various Indian animals:**

1. The Dhole (Asiatic wild dog) is classified as Vulnerable by the IUCN.
2. The Himalayan Musk Deer is listed under Appendix II of CITES.
3. The Pygmy Hog is found in several protected areas across North India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Dhole is classified as Endangered (EN), not Vulnerable (VU), by the IUCN.  The distinction between EN and VU is significant in conservation planning.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Himalayan Musk Deer is listed under Appendix I of CITES, indicating a higher level of threat and the need for stricter trade controls. Appendix II includes species that may become threatened if trade is not controlled.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Pygmy Hog is primarily found in Manas Wildlife Sanctuary in Assam, with extremely limited distribution and not across North India.  The restricted range highlights its vulnerability to habitat loss and other threats.


**5. With reference to the Indian Forest (Amendment) Act, 2017, consider the following statements:**

1. The Act redefined the definition of "trees" to include palm trees.
2. The Act explicitly excluded canes from the definition of "trees".
3. The Act removed bamboo from the definition of "trees" which were previously included in the definition of trees.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The 2017 amendment did not include palm trees in the definition of "trees". The specific plants included or excluded are subject to detailed legal interpretation and vary based on regional contexts.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The amendment did not explicitly address canes in its definition of trees.  The focus was primarily on bamboo and its implications for forest management.

Statement 3 is correct. A significant change introduced by the Indian Forest (Amendment) Act, 2017, was the removal of bamboo from the definition of "trees," which had implications for its regulation and management.  This deregulation aimed to promote bamboo cultivation and its use in various sectors.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the Indian Forest (Amendment) Act, 2017, consider the following statements:**

1. The Act explicitly defines "tree" to include all woody perennial plants exceeding a specified height.
2. The Act excludes palm trees from the legal definition of "tree" in non-forest areas.
3. The amendment aimed to clarify the definition of trees to prevent ambiguity in forest conservation efforts.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

The Indian Forest (Amendment) Act, 2017 primarily focused on clarifying ambiguities surrounding the definition of "trees" within the context of forest conservation.  Statement 3 accurately reflects this core objective. Statement 1 is incorrect because the Act doesn't provide a universally applicable height threshold for all woody perennial plants to be considered trees. The definition can vary depending on the specific context and regional regulations. Similarly, statement 2 is inaccurate; while the Act might exclude certain plants like palms in specific non-forest areas, it doesn't do so universally.  The exclusion of certain plants from the definition of “tree” is often based on local ecological factors and land use practices, not a blanket exclusion by the Act itself.  Therefore, only statement 3 correctly captures the essence of the 2017 amendment.


**2. With reference to the impact of global warming, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Kyoto Protocol primarily focused on mitigating methane emissions to curb global warming.
2.  Increased frequency of forest fires is a direct consequence of global warming, leading to further carbon emissions.
3.  The thawing of permafrost and increased wildfires act as positive feedback loops, exacerbating global warming.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

While the Kyoto Protocol did address greenhouse gas emissions, its primary focus wasn't solely on methane.  It addressed multiple greenhouse gases, including carbon dioxide.  Therefore, statement 1 is incorrect. Statement 2 is partially true; increased forest fires are linked to global warming, but the causal relationship is complex and not always a direct consequence.  Other factors like human activity and drought conditions also contribute significantly.  Statement 3 accurately describes a key aspect of global warming: positive feedback loops.  Thawing permafrost releases methane, a potent greenhouse gas, and increased wildfires release significant amounts of carbon dioxide, both accelerating the warming process. Thus, only statement 3 provides a completely accurate description of a key mechanism in global warming.


**3. With reference to India's National Parks and their conservation efforts, consider the following statements:**

1. The Jim Corbett National Park, established in 1936, is primarily known for its conservation of the one-horned rhinoceros.
2. The Kaziranga National Park is a UNESCO World Heritage Site renowned for its high density of the Indian rhinoceros.
3. The Gir National Park is mainly dedicated to the conservation of Asiatic lions.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Jim Corbett National Park was India's first national park, its primary focus is on tiger conservation, not the one-horned rhinoceros. That species is primarily found in Kaziranga. Statement 2 is correct; Kaziranga National Park is indeed a UNESCO World Heritage Site and is famous for its large population of one-horned rhinoceros. Statement 3 is also correct; Gir National Park is the only habitat of Asiatic lions in India and is dedicated to their protection.  Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are accurate.


**4. With reference to the Ganga River, consider the following statements:**

1. The Ganga River originates from the Gangotri Glacier and flows through the city of Patna.
2.  The Chambal River is a major tributary of the Ganga, joining it at Prayagraj.
3. The Hooghly River is a distributary of the Ganga.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct. The Ganga does originate from the Gangotri Glacier and flows through Patna.  However, statement 2 is incorrect; the Chambal River is a tributary of the Yamuna River, which in turn is a tributary of the Ganga.  The confluence is not at Prayagraj. Statement 3 is correct; the Hooghly River is a major distributary of the Ganga.  Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are accurate.


**5. With reference to Biodiversity Hotspots in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Western Ghats and Sri Lanka biodiversity hotspot includes significant populations of Asian Elephants and Indian Tigers.
2. The Himalaya biodiversity hotspot is characterized by high levels of endemism in freshwater turtle species.
3. The Sundaland biodiversity hotspot is significantly threatened by industrial forestry, particularly palm and rubber plantations.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct; the Western Ghats and Sri Lanka hotspot is indeed rich in biodiversity, including significant populations of Asian elephants and tigers. Statement 2 is incorrect; while the Himalaya hotspot is rich in biodiversity, high endemism in freshwater turtles is more characteristic of the Indo-Burma hotspot.  Statement 3 is correct; the Sundaland hotspot faces significant threats from industrial forestry, particularly palm oil and rubber plantations. Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are accurate.


These questions aim to test in-depth knowledge and understanding of the topics, requiring more than superficial recall. The distractors are designed to be plausible, based on related but ultimately incorrect information, thus increasing the difficulty level and making simple guessing less effective.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the geographical features of the Rann of Kachchh:**

1. The Luni River, originating in the Aravalli Range, empties into the Rann of Kachchh, contributing significantly to its salinity.
2. The Rann of Kachchh is a vast, low-lying coastal plain that extends from the Thar Desert, characterized by seasonal inundation.
3.  The Rann of Kachchh's unique geological formation is primarily attributed to volcanic activity and subsequent erosion over millennia.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Luni River indeed flows through the Thar Desert and eventually reaches the Rann of Kachchh. While its contribution to the overall salinity is significant, the primary source of salinity is the evaporation of seawater in this low-lying area.  The statement is not entirely precise in its description of the Luni's origin (it doesn't solely originate in the Aravalli range, but also receives tributaries from other areas), but it's close enough to be considered factually correct in the context of the question.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Rann of Kachchh is a large, flat, coastal plain that stretches from the Thar Desert.  The seasonal inundation is a key characteristic, transforming the landscape from a vast salt desert to a shallow inland sea during monsoon season.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Rann of Kachchh's formation is primarily due to tectonic activity, specifically subsidence and the deposition of sediments by rivers over a long geological period. Volcanic activity is not a major factor in its formation.  This statement presents a significant misconception about the region's geology.


**2. With reference to the impact of Diclofenac on vulture populations in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The decline in vulture populations is solely attributable to the widespread use of Diclofenac, a non-steroidal anti-inflammatory drug (NSAID).
2.  Diclofenac, when ingested by vultures through scavenging carcasses of treated animals, causes visceral gout and renal failure, leading to high mortality rates among vultures.
3. The use of Meloxicam, a safer alternative to Diclofenac, has completely reversed the decline in Indian vulture populations.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Diclofenac is the primary factor driving the decline of vulture populations in India, it's not the sole cause.  Other factors, such as habitat loss and human persecution, have also contributed to the overall population decline. The statement oversimplifies a complex ecological issue.

Statement 2 is correct.  Diclofenac's impact on vultures is well-documented.  Vultures feeding on carcasses of livestock treated with Diclofenac suffer from severe kidney and liver damage, resulting in high mortality.  The statement accurately describes the mechanism of Diclofenac's toxicity.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While Meloxicam is a safer alternative and its use is encouraged, it hasn't completely reversed the decline. The recovery of vulture populations is a slow and ongoing process requiring sustained efforts beyond simply replacing Diclofenac. The statement presents an overly optimistic and inaccurate assessment of the situation.


**3. With reference to the Kaziranga National Park, consider the following statements:**

1. The Kaziranga National Park is situated in the Brahmaputra Valley, characterized by grasslands and savannas.
2. The primary conservation focus of the Kaziranga National Park is the protection of the one-horned rhinoceros, with significant populations of other endangered species like tigers and elephants also present.
3. The park's unique biodiversity is primarily threatened by human encroachment and habitat degradation caused by excessive agricultural activities within the park boundaries.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Kaziranga National Park is located in the Brahmaputra Valley.  Its landscape is indeed dominated by grasslands and savannas, although there are also patches of forest.

Statement 2 is correct. The park is renowned for its one-horned rhinoceros population, which is a major focus of conservation efforts. However, it also supports other significant populations of endangered species, including tigers and Asian elephants.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While human encroachment and habitat loss are significant threats, excessive agricultural activities *within* the park boundaries are not the primary cause. The main threats stem from encroachment on the park's periphery, leading to habitat fragmentation and poaching, along with the impact of floods on the park's ecosystem.  The statement misrepresents the nature of the threats.



**4. Consider the following statements about the Odisha state in India:**

1. The Hirakud Dam, constructed across the Mahanadi River, primarily serves the purpose of flood control and irrigation in the Mahanadi delta region.
2.  Odisha's coastline is characterized by extensive mangrove forests, particularly in the Bhitarkanika National Park, playing a crucial role in coastal protection and biodiversity.
3. Odisha's economy is heavily reliant on agriculture, with rice cultivation being the dominant agricultural activity, and minimal contribution from the mining sector.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  The Hirakud Dam on the Mahanadi River is a significant irrigation and flood control structure, benefitting a large agricultural area in the Mahanadi delta.

Statement 2 is also correct. Odisha has a substantial coastline with significant mangrove cover, especially in the Bhitarkanika National Park.  These mangroves are important for coastal protection and harbor rich biodiversity.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While agriculture is a significant part of Odisha's economy, the state is also a major producer of minerals, particularly bauxite and iron ore.  The mining sector contributes substantially to the state's GDP.  The statement underestimates the importance of the mining sector.


**5. With reference to the Sundarbans mangrove forest, consider the following statements:**

1. The Sundarbans, located primarily in West Bengal, India, is the largest single block of tidal halophytic mangroves in the world and is a UNESCO World Heritage Site.
2.  The Sundarbans' unique ecosystem is threatened primarily by rising sea levels, salinity intrusion, and deforestation.
3. The endangered Royal Bengal Tiger is the flagship species of the Sundarbans, with its population showing a significant increase in recent years due to successful conservation efforts.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Sundarbans is indeed the world's largest single block of tidal mangrove forest and holds UNESCO World Heritage Site status. The primary location is in West Bengal, though it extends into Bangladesh.

Statement 2 is also correct. The Sundarbans faces severe threats from rising sea levels, salinity intrusion, and both legal and illegal deforestation. These factors significantly impact the ecosystem's health and the survival of its inhabitants.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Royal Bengal tiger is the flagship species, recent population data do not consistently show a significant *increase* in recent years.  The population fluctuates, and conservation efforts are ongoing to ensure its survival amidst the environmental threats facing the Sundarbans.  The statement presents an oversimplification of a complex conservation issue.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements:**

1. The Bannerghatta Biological Park in Bangalore houses a significant population of Asiatic lions.
2.  The Kochi-Mangalore-Bangalore pipeline directly supplies water to the Bannerghatta Biological Park.
3. Shahji, while attempting to establish a principality in Bangalore, significantly impacted the development of the Textile Industry there.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (d)


**Explanation:**

None of the statements are entirely correct. Let's analyze each:

1. **Incorrect:** The provided text mentions that Bannerghatta Biological Park shelters lions and Indian tigers.  However, it doesn't specify the *Asiatic* lion, which is found primarily in Gujarat's Gir National Park.  The question uses a distractor by substituting "Asiatic lions" for the factually correct "lions" and "Indian tigers," introducing ambiguity and requiring precise knowledge of animal distribution.

2. **Incorrect:** The text mentions the Kochi-Mangalore-Bangalore pipeline, but there's no information linking it directly to the water supply of Bannerghatta Biological Park. The statement creates a false connection between seemingly related geographical entities, typical of UPSC distractors.

3. **Incorrect:** While Shahji attempted to establish a principality in Bangalore, and Bangalore is a center of the Textile Industry, the text doesn't establish a direct causal link between Shahji's actions and the industry's development. This statement uses a distractor by implying a correlation where none is explicitly stated, testing the candidate's ability to avoid making unwarranted assumptions.  The question plays on the candidate's general knowledge about historical figures and economic activities, making it less straightforward.


**2. With reference to the geographical features of Jharkhand, consider the following statements:**

**Correct Answer:** (b)


**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The text confirms the Subarnarekha River's origin in Jharkhand and its course through Odisha and West Bengal.  This is a straightforward factual recall question.

Statement 2 is partially correct, creating a distractor. While the text provides Jharkhand's forest cover, it doesn't directly state its contribution to India's forest density. The statement tests the candidate's understanding of the implication of the data, requiring them to evaluate the significance of the given area in relation to India's overall forest cover.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The question uses a distractor by introducing Parasnath, a known religious site, as the highest peak, though the text does not specify the highest peak in Jharkhand. The candidate needs to differentiate between a religious site and a geographical feature.


**3. With reference to the state of Nagaland, consider the following statements:**

2.  The Hornbill Festival, celebrated in Nagaland, showcases the traditions of the Kukis, a major ethnic group inhabiting both Nagaland and Mizoram.
3. The Guwahati High Court has jurisdiction over Nagaland, but not over Mizoram.

(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (d)


**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The text states Nagaland's forest cover is 74% of its geographical area and Mizoram's is 85%. The statement plays on the similar nature of the two states, requiring precise recall of the percentage.

Statement 2 is partially correct, but misleading. While Hornbill Festival is celebrated in Nagaland, and Kukis inhabit both Nagaland and Mizoram, the text doesn't explicitly state that the Kukis' traditions are the *primary* focus of the Hornbill Festival. The statement acts as a distractor by presenting a partially true but incomplete picture, requiring analytical skills.

Statement 3 is correct. The text clearly states that Guwahati High Court has jurisdiction over Nagaland and Mizoram.  This statement is a straightforward factual recall question.  The distractor attempts to make the examinee believe that Guwahati High Court has jurisdiction only over Nagaland.


**4. Consider the following statements about the state of Gujarat:**

1. The Asiatic lion population in Gujarat, estimated at 650 in 2017, is the only remaining wild population of this subspecies in India.
