It encompassed a wide range of sustainable development goals, including poverty eradication, environmental protection, and economic growth. Ocean acidification was one of several environmental concerns discussed, but not the main focus.


**2. Consider the following statements:**

1.  Increased plant growth due to elevated atmospheric CO2 concentrations is a phenomenon known as "carbon fertilization," directly contributing to increased global warming.
2.  Thermal sensors utilize infrared radiation to detect temperature variations, making them crucial tools in various fields including climate monitoring and remote sensing.
3.  Abandoned and uneconomic coal seams, depleted oil and gas reservoirs, and subterranean deep saline formations are all potential sites for carbon sequestration, but their effectiveness varies depending on geological factors.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct. Thermal sensors indeed leverage infrared radiation's properties to measure temperature differences.  This principle underpins their wide use in various applications, including environmental monitoring, where they help track temperature changes across various scales.

Statement 3 is also correct.  These geological formations offer potential for storing captured CO2, thereby sequestering it from the atmosphere. However, the suitability of each site depends on factors like geological stability, porosity, and permeability, influencing the long-term security of the stored carbon.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While increased plant growth due to higher CO2 levels is termed "carbon fertilization," it does *not* directly contribute to *increased* global warming.  It is a complex feedback mechanism.  Although plants absorb CO2, the overall effect on global warming is not straightforward and depends on several other factors such as the plant's lifespan, the type of plant, and the overall carbon cycle dynamics.  The increased growth can partially offset warming, but it doesn't directly increase it.


**3. With reference to the impact of solar radiation, consider the following statements:**

1.  High levels of solar radiation are a primary cause of coral bleaching, leading to the degradation of coral reef ecosystems.
2.  Solar radiation is essential for photosynthesis, the fundamental biological process that sustains most life on Earth.
3.  The Greenhouse effect involves the absorption and re-radiation of infrared radiation, not solar radiation, by atmospheric gases to warm the planet.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct. Solar radiation is the primary energy source driving photosynthesis, the process by which plants and other organisms convert light energy into chemical energy, forming the base of most food chains.

Statement 3 is also correct. The Greenhouse effect focuses on the interaction of infrared radiation (heat) with greenhouse gases in the atmosphere.  These gases absorb outgoing infrared radiation, trapping heat and warming the planet.  Solar radiation is the initial energy input, but the Greenhouse effect itself operates through infrared radiation.

Statement 1 is incorrect. While high levels of solar radiation can contribute to stress on coral reefs, it's not the *primary* cause of coral bleaching.  Coral bleaching is mainly caused by increased water temperatures, often associated with climate change, which leads to the expulsion of symbiotic algae from coral tissues.  Although high solar radiation can exacerbate the effects of warming, it's not the direct and primary cause.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding climate change mitigation:**

1.  The "Great Green Wall" initiative aims to combat desertification and land degradation, indirectly contributing to carbon sequestration through afforestation and improved land management practices.
2.  The National Mission for a Green India (in India) focuses primarily on reducing greenhouse gas emissions through the promotion of renewable energy sources such as solar and wind power.
3.  Ocean deoxygenation, a consequence of anthropogenic CO2 emissions, is a significant environmental issue that exacerbates the impacts of global warming but is not directly related to the process of carbon sequestration.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Great Green Wall initiative, a large-scale afforestation project, aims to combat desertification.  This indirectly contributes to carbon sequestration as trees absorb CO2 during photosynthesis. Improved land management further enhances carbon storage in soils.

Statement 3 is correct. Ocean deoxygenation, the reduction of dissolved oxygen in the ocean, is linked to increased CO2 emissions.  Warmer water holds less dissolved oxygen, and ocean acidification (also caused by increased CO2) affects marine life and ecosystems.  However, this process itself is not directly involved in carbon sequestration; it's a consequence of excess atmospheric CO2.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The National Mission for a Green India primarily focuses on enhancing forest cover and biodiversity, not directly on promoting renewable energy.  While afforestation can contribute to carbon sequestration, the mission's core aim is ecological restoration and biodiversity conservation.  Renewable energy promotion falls under other national missions in India.


**5. With reference to the sources and impacts of greenhouse gases, consider the following statements:**

1.  Nitrous oxide (N2O), a potent greenhouse gas, is primarily emitted from agricultural activities, particularly through the use of nitrogen-based fertilizers.
2.  Methane (CH4) emissions from livestock, mainly through enteric fermentation (belching), contribute significantly to global warming, having a higher global warming potential than CO2 over a 20-year timeframe.
3.  Black carbon, or soot, is a short-lived climate pollutant that directly absorbs solar radiation, contributing to warming but having a much longer atmospheric lifetime than CO2.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Nitrous oxide (N2O) is a potent greenhouse gas, and agricultural activities, especially the use of nitrogen fertilizers, are a major source of its emissions.  The nitrogen cycle is significantly impacted by human activities, leading to increased N2O release into the atmosphere.

Statement 2 is correct. Methane (CH4) from livestock is a significant contributor to global warming. Enteric fermentation in ruminant animals (like cows) is a primary source of methane emissions.  CH4 has a much higher global warming potential than CO2 over shorter timeframes (like 20 years).

Statement 3 is incorrect. While black carbon does absorb solar radiation and contribute to warming, its atmospheric lifetime is *much shorter* than that of CO2, not longer.  Black carbon remains in the atmosphere for days to weeks, while CO2 persists for centuries.  The short lifetime makes it a significant but short-term contributor to warming.

**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Montreal Protocol:**

1. The Montreal Protocol's primary objective is the reduction of greenhouse gas emissions contributing to global warming.
2.  The Kigali Amendment to the Montreal Protocol focuses on phasing down hydrofluorocarbons (HFCs).
3. The Vienna Convention established a framework for international cooperation on ozone layer protection, but didn't include specific regulations on ozone-depleting substances.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Montreal Protocol's success in reducing ozone-depleting substances has indirectly helped mitigate climate change (as some ODS are also greenhouse gases), its primary focus is not on greenhouse gas emissions in general.  The Kyoto Protocol and the Paris Agreement are the major international treaties addressing greenhouse gas emissions directly.

Statement 2 is correct. The Kigali Amendment, adopted in 2016, is a significant addition to the Montreal Protocol.  Its key goal is the gradual reduction and eventual phase-out of hydrofluorocarbons (HFCs), potent greenhouse gases that were introduced as replacements for ozone-depleting substances. This demonstrates a proactive approach to addressing climate change while building upon the success of the original protocol.

Statement 3 is correct. The Vienna Convention for the Protection of the Ozone Layer, adopted in 1985, laid the groundwork for the Montreal Protocol.  It established a framework for international cooperation on ozone layer protection, but lacked the specific regulations and control measures that were later incorporated into the Montreal Protocol.  The Montreal Protocol essentially built upon the Vienna Convention's framework, providing the specific legal mechanisms for phasing out ozone-depleting substances.


**2. With reference to the Kyoto Protocol, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Kyoto Protocol legally binds all UNFCCC signatory nations to reduce their greenhouse gas emissions by specific targets.
2.  The Clean Development Mechanism (CDM) under the Kyoto Protocol allows developed countries to invest in emission reduction projects in developing countries to meet their emission reduction targets.
3. The United States ratified the Kyoto Protocol and actively participated in its implementation throughout its duration.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Kyoto Protocol did not legally bind all UNFCCC signatory nations equally.  It established differentiated responsibilities, with Annex I countries (developed nations) having legally binding emission reduction targets, while developing countries (non-Annex I) had voluntary commitments.  This principle of "common but differentiated responsibilities" is a core element of the UNFCCC and its subsequent protocols.

Statement 2 is correct. The Clean Development Mechanism (CDM) was a key flexible mechanism under the Kyoto Protocol. It allowed developed countries to invest in emission reduction projects in developing countries, earning carbon credits that could be used to meet their own emission reduction targets. This mechanism aimed to promote sustainable development and technology transfer while achieving global emission reductions.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The United States, a major emitter of greenhouse gases, signed the Kyoto Protocol but never ratified it.  Consequently, the US did not participate in its legally binding emission reduction targets. This lack of US participation was a significant factor limiting the overall effectiveness of the Kyoto Protocol.



**3. With reference to the impact of increased global temperatures, consider the following statements:**

1. A global temperature increase exceeding 3°C above pre-industrial levels would result in the complete and permanent disappearance of all global wetlands.
2.  Increased global temperatures beyond 3°C above pre-industrial levels would lead to widespread coral mortality.
3.  If global temperatures rise beyond 3°C above pre-industrial levels, terrestrial biomes would become net carbon sources.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While a global temperature increase of 3°C or more would severely impact wetlands, leading to significant loss and alteration of these ecosystems, it is inaccurate to state that *all* global wetlands would permanently disappear.  The extent of wetland loss would vary greatly depending on location, specific characteristics of the wetland, and other interacting factors.

Statement 2 is correct.  Coral reefs are highly sensitive to temperature changes. A 3°C increase above pre-industrial levels would cause widespread coral bleaching and mortality, severely damaging these vital marine ecosystems. This is due to the disruption of the symbiotic relationship between corals and the algae that live within them.

Statement 3 is correct.  At a global temperature increase exceeding 3°C above pre-industrial levels, many terrestrial ecosystems would likely transition from being net carbon sinks (absorbing more carbon than they release) to net carbon sources (releasing more carbon than they absorb). This is because higher temperatures would accelerate decomposition rates, increase forest fires, and reduce the capacity of plants to absorb carbon dioxide.  This positive feedback loop would further exacerbate global warming.


**4.  With reference to ozone depletion, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Antarctic ozone hole is primarily caused by the presence of prominent tropospheric turbulence and the inflow of chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs).
2.  Chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs) are used in the production of tubeless tires and as pressurizing agents in aerosol cans.
3. Polar stratospheric clouds (PSCs) play a crucial role in accelerating ozone depletion in polar regions.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the inflow of CFCs is a crucial factor in ozone depletion, tropospheric turbulence does not directly contribute to the formation of the Antarctic ozone hole. The primary reason for the ozone hole's formation is the combination of the polar stratospheric vortex, extremely low temperatures, and the presence of polar stratospheric clouds (PSCs), which provide a surface for chemical reactions involving CFCs to destroy ozone.

Statement 2 is partially correct. While CFCs were used as pressurizing agents in aerosol cans, they were *not* used in the production of tubeless tires.  The use of CFCs was prevalent in refrigeration, air conditioning, and foam-blowing agents.  This statement uses a distractor to test the candidate's specific knowledge.

Statement 3 is correct. Polar stratospheric clouds (PSCs) are crucial to the ozone depletion process in polar regions.  These clouds form at very low temperatures and contain particles that facilitate chemical reactions involving CFCs, leading to the destruction of ozone molecules.  The presence of PSCs significantly amplifies the ozone-depleting potential of CFCs.



**5. With reference to the sources of methane emissions, consider the following statements:**

1.  Rice cultivation is a significant source of methane emissions, primarily due to anaerobic decomposition in flooded paddy fields.
2.  Enteric fermentation in livestock (e.g., cows and sheep) is not a major source of atmospheric methane.
3.  The decomposition of organic matter in landfills is a significant source of methane emissions.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Rice paddies are renowned for being significant sources of methane emissions. The flooded conditions create an anaerobic environment, ideal for methanogenic archaea to thrive and produce methane during the decomposition of organic matter. This is a well-established fact in climate science.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Enteric fermentation in the digestive systems of ruminant animals (cows, sheep, goats, etc.) is a major source of atmospheric methane.  These animals produce methane as a byproduct of their digestive processes, and their large populations contribute substantially to global methane emissions.

Statement 3 is correct.  Landfills are significant sources of methane emissions.  The anaerobic decomposition of organic waste in landfills generates large quantities of methane, a potent greenhouse gas.  This is a major environmental concern, and efforts are underway to capture and utilize this methane or to reduce its generation.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is followed by its correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements about the stratosphere:**

1. The stratosphere exhibits a negative lapse rate, meaning temperature increases with altitude.
2. Polar Stratospheric Clouds (PSCs) are exclusively found in the troposphere, influencing weather patterns.
3. The ozone layer, crucial for absorbing UV radiation, is entirely located within the stratosphere.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Unlike the troposphere where temperature generally decreases with altitude, the stratosphere displays a temperature inversion due to the absorption of UV radiation by the ozone layer.  This leads to a positive lapse rate (temperature increasing with altitude).

Statement 2 is incorrect. PSCs are indeed associated with ozone depletion, but they are specifically located in the lower stratosphere, particularly above the polar regions, not the troposphere. The troposphere is the lowest layer of the atmosphere where weather phenomena primarily occur.

Statement 3 is largely correct. While a small portion of the ozone layer extends into the lower mesosphere, the vast majority and its highest concentration are found within the stratosphere.  The statement's simplification is acceptable for the purpose of the question.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are correct.  Option (b) is the most appropriate answer.  Options (a), (c), and (d) misrepresent the atmospheric layering and the characteristics of PSCs.


**2. With reference to phytoplankton and photosynthesis, consider the following statements:**

1. Phytoplankton, primarily inhabiting aquatic habitats, are the sole producers of dimethylsulfide (DMS).
2. Photosynthesis in phytoplankton requires sunlight and nutrients but is independent of the carbon cycle.
3. Zooplankton directly consume phytoplankton, forming a crucial link in the marine food web.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While phytoplankton are significant producers of DMS, they are not the *sole* source. Other marine organisms also contribute to DMS production.  The statement oversimplifies a complex biogeochemical process.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Photosynthesis, whether in phytoplankton or other plants, is intrinsically linked to the carbon cycle. It utilizes carbon dioxide (CO2) from the atmosphere and incorporates it into organic molecules, thus playing a vital role in regulating atmospheric CO2 levels.

Statement 3 is correct. Zooplankton are primary consumers in many aquatic ecosystems, feeding directly on phytoplankton. This predator-prey relationship is a fundamental aspect of marine food webs.


Therefore, only statement 3 is correct, making option (c) the correct choice. Options (a), (b), and (d) contain inaccuracies regarding the sources of DMS, the role of the carbon cycle in phytoplankton photosynthesis, and the simplification of the marine food web.


**3. With reference to the impacts of global warming, consider the following statements:**

1. Global warming directly causes ozone depletion in the stratosphere, leading to increased UV radiation.
2.  The melting of glaciers and thermal expansion of ocean water are the only contributors to sea-level rise.
3. The increased frequency and intensity of heat waves are a direct consequence of global warming.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While both global warming and ozone depletion are environmental concerns, they are largely independent processes.  Ozone depletion is primarily caused by the release of ozone-depleting substances (ODS), such as chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs), not directly by global warming.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Sea-level rise is a complex phenomenon influenced by multiple factors.  While glacial melt and thermal expansion are major contributors, other factors like changes in land water storage and variations in ocean currents also play a role.  The statement oversimplifies a complex issue.

Statement 3 is correct.  Increased heat waves are a direct and well-documented consequence of global warming, resulting from the increased trapping of heat in the atmosphere.

Therefore, only statement 3 is correct, making option (b) the correct answer. Options (a), (c), and (d) include inaccurate statements about the relationship between global warming and ozone depletion and the complexities of sea-level rise.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding methane (CH4):**

1.  Methane is a more potent greenhouse gas than carbon dioxide (CO2) on a per-molecule basis, but has a shorter atmospheric lifetime.
2.  The primary source of atmospheric methane is the combustion of fossil fuels in power plants.
3.  Methane emissions from agriculture, particularly from livestock and rice cultivation, contribute significantly to global warming.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Methane has a much higher global warming potential (GWP) than CO2 over shorter timeframes (e.g., 20 years), but it breaks down in the atmosphere more quickly than CO2. This means its overall warming impact is complex and depends on the timeframe considered.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While fossil fuel combustion does release methane, it's not the primary source.  Agriculture (livestock, rice paddies) and natural sources (wetlands) are much larger contributors to atmospheric methane.

Statement 3 is correct. Agricultural practices, particularly livestock farming (enteric fermentation) and rice cultivation (anaerobic conditions in paddy fields), are major sources of methane emissions, significantly contributing to the greenhouse effect and global warming.

Therefore, only statements 1 and 3 are correct, making option (b) the appropriate answer. Option (a), (c), and (d) present misinterpretations of the relative importance of methane sources and its atmospheric lifetime.


**5. With reference to the sources of nitrous oxide (N2O), consider the following statements:**

1.  Nitrous oxide is primarily released into the atmosphere through volcanic eruptions.
2.  The use of nitrogen-based fertilizers in agriculture is a significant source of N2O emissions.
3.  Burning of fossil fuels contributes negligibly to N2O emissions compared to agricultural sources.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While volcanoes do release some N2O, it's not the primary source.  Human activities, especially agriculture, are responsible for the majority of N2O emissions.

Statement 2 is correct.  The application of nitrogen-based fertilizers in agriculture significantly contributes to N2O emissions.  The microbial processes in soil involved in nitrogen cycling release N2O as a byproduct.

Statement 3 is correct.  While fossil fuel combustion does release some N2O, agricultural sources (fertilizers, livestock) are far more significant contributors to global N2O emissions.

Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are correct, making (c) the correct answer. Options (a), (b), and (d) misrepresent the major sources of atmospheric nitrous oxide.

**1. Consider the following statements regarding greenhouse gases:**

1.  Methane's 20-year global warming potential is significantly higher than that of carbon dioxide, making it a more potent greenhouse gas.
2.  Nitrous oxide persists in the atmosphere for a considerably longer duration than methane, contributing to its cumulative warming effect.
3.  Water vapor, while a potent greenhouse gas, is primarily a feedback mechanism rather than a direct driver of climate change.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Methane (CH₄) has a much higher global warming potential (GWP) than carbon dioxide (CO₂) over shorter timeframes (e.g., 20 years). While CO₂ has a longer atmospheric lifetime, methane's potent short-term warming effect makes it a significant contributor to global warming.  The provided text explicitly states that methane's 20-year GWP is 84 times higher than CO₂, highlighting its potency.

Statement 2 is also correct. Nitrous oxide (N₂O) has a considerably longer atmospheric lifetime (around 120 years) compared to methane (around 12 years). This means N₂O remains in the atmosphere for a much longer time, contributing to a sustained warming effect.  The text supports this, indicating N₂O's long atmospheric lifetime and its contribution to global warming.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While water vapor is indeed a potent greenhouse gas, its concentration in the atmosphere is largely determined by temperature.  Warmer temperatures lead to increased evaporation and higher water vapor concentrations, amplifying the warming effect (positive feedback). However,  the initial increase in atmospheric temperature is primarily driven by other greenhouse gases like CO₂, CH₄, and N₂O. Water vapor acts as a feedback mechanism, enhancing the warming caused by these other gases, not as a primary driver.


**2. With reference to the sources and impacts of greenhouse gases, consider the following statements:**

1.  Deforestation significantly contributes to increased atmospheric carbon dioxide levels primarily through the release of stored carbon during tree decomposition and combustion.
2.  The burning of fossil fuels is a major source of both carbon dioxide and nitrous oxide emissions, contributing significantly to global warming.
3.  Methane emissions from livestock primarily originate from enteric fermentation, a digestive process in ruminants that produces methane as a byproduct.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Deforestation leads to a net increase in atmospheric CO₂.  Trees store vast amounts of carbon. When forests are cleared, this stored carbon is released into the atmosphere, both through the decomposition of organic matter and often through the burning of the cleared vegetation. This significantly contributes to the enhanced greenhouse effect.

Statement 2 is correct. The combustion of fossil fuels (coal, oil, and natural gas) is a dominant source of CO₂ emissions.  However, it is also a significant source of nitrous oxide (N₂O) emissions, although not as large as CO₂.  Fossil fuel combustion processes can generate N₂O as a byproduct, adding to its contribution to global warming.

Statement 3 is correct.  The text explicitly states that methane emissions from livestock are primarily a result of enteric fermentation, a digestive process unique to ruminant animals (like cows and sheep) where microorganisms break down complex carbohydrates, producing methane as a byproduct.  This process is a far more significant source of methane from livestock than flatulence (cow farts).



**3. Consider the following statements regarding the impact of climate change:**

1.  Increased frequency and intensity of El Niño events are linked to anthropogenic climate change, influencing global weather patterns.
2.  The melting of glaciers and polar ice caps, driven by global warming, is a primary contributor to rising sea levels.
3.  The increase in condensation nuclei, largely due to pollution, causes disproportionately high monsoonal rainfall in urban areas compared to rural areas.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d) 1, 2, and 3

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The provided text explicitly connects the increased incidence of El Niño events to anthropogenic climate change, suggesting a link between human-induced warming and the alteration of weather patterns.

Statement 2 is correct.  Rising global temperatures, a key consequence of climate change, directly contribute to the melting of glaciers and polar ice, leading to a significant increase in the volume of water in the oceans. This thermal expansion of water, coupled with glacial melt, is a primary driver of sea level rise.

Statement 3 is correct. The text details how increased condensation nuclei from pollution increase water vapor condensation, leading to higher rainfall in urban areas. This disproportionate rainfall, in turn, can cause flooding in urban centers while leaving rural agricultural areas with less water, contributing to drought conditions.


**4. With reference to ozone depletion, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Antarctic ozone hole is primarily a springtime phenomenon, associated with the unique meteorological conditions of the polar vortex and the formation of polar stratospheric clouds (PSCs).
2.  Chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs),  once widely used in refrigeration and other applications, are major ozone-depleting substances (ODS) that release chlorine atoms which catalyze ozone destruction.
3.  Methane, while a greenhouse gas, plays a significant role in the direct depletion of the ozone layer in the polar regions.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The text clearly explains that the Antarctic ozone hole is most prominent during springtime, due to the unique combination of the polar vortex and the formation of PSCs which provide surfaces for chemical reactions that deplete ozone.  The Arctic ozone depletion is less significant due to weaker vortex and higher temperatures.

Statement 2 is correct. The text specifically identifies CFCs as major ODS, explaining how their photodissociation releases chlorine atoms which act as catalysts, destroying ozone molecules in a chain reaction.  This is the primary mechanism of ozone depletion caused by human activities.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While methane is a potent greenhouse gas and can indirectly affect atmospheric chemistry, it is not a primary ozone-depleting substance. Methane does not directly break down ozone in the way that CFCs do;  the role of halogens (like chlorine from CFCs) in ozone depletion is paramount.  Methane's impact on ozone is indirect and far less significant than the effect of CFCs.

**1. Consider the following statements about Nitrous Oxide (N₂O):**

1.  N₂O is a more potent greenhouse gas than Carbon Dioxide (CO₂) on a per-molecule basis, but has a shorter atmospheric lifetime.
2.  Agricultural practices, particularly the use of nitrogen-based fertilizers, are a significant source of anthropogenic N₂O emissions.
3.  N₂O contributes to the depletion of the stratospheric ozone layer, unlike most other greenhouse gases.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct. While N₂O is indeed a more potent greenhouse gas than CO₂ in terms of its global warming potential (GWP), its atmospheric lifetime is considerably longer than that of methane, not shorter.  Methane has a much shorter atmospheric lifetime than N₂O.  The GWP of N₂O is significantly higher than that of CO2, meaning it traps significantly more heat per molecule. However, its concentration in the atmosphere is lower than CO2.

Statement 2 is correct.  Agriculture is a major source of N₂O emissions, primarily from the microbial breakdown of nitrogen-containing fertilizers in soil.  This process, called nitrification and denitrification, releases N₂O into the atmosphere.  Other sources include livestock manure management and industrial processes.

Statement 3 is incorrect. N₂O does contribute to global warming as a greenhouse gas, but its role in stratospheric ozone depletion is relatively minor compared to other ozone-depleting substances (ODS) like chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs) and halons. While N₂O can catalytically destroy ozone in the stratosphere, its impact is significantly less than that of the ODS regulated under the Montreal Protocol.


**2. Consider the following statements regarding Bhutan:**

1. Bhutan's Gross National Happiness (GNH) index prioritizes environmental sustainability alongside economic growth.
2.  Bhutan shares a significant portion of its border with Nepal.
3. Bhutan's economy is heavily reliant on hydropower exports to India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Bhutan's unique development model, centered around the GNH index, places significant emphasis on environmental conservation and ecological balance, recognizing their crucial role in overall well-being. This contrasts with purely GDP-focused development models.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Bhutan shares its borders with India and China, not Nepal.  Nepal is geographically separated from Bhutan by the Indian state of Sikkim.

Statement 3 is correct.  Hydropower generation and export constitute a major pillar of Bhutan's economy, with India being the primary recipient of this electricity. This energy cooperation strengthens bilateral relations and contributes significantly to Bhutan's revenue stream.


**3. With reference to the Greenhouse Effect, consider the following statements:**

1. Water vapor is the most abundant greenhouse gas in the Earth's atmosphere, accounting for the largest percentage of the greenhouse effect.
2.  Methane (CH₄) has a significantly higher global warming potential (GWP) than carbon dioxide (CO₂) over a 20-year timeframe.
3.  The increase in atmospheric concentrations of greenhouse gases is primarily due to natural processes, such as volcanic eruptions.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While water vapor is a significant greenhouse gas and its concentration is high, it's not the most abundant. Carbon dioxide (CO₂) holds that position, although water vapor's contribution to the greenhouse effect is substantial and is amplified by a warming climate (positive feedback).  Water vapor's concentration is highly variable depending on temperature and humidity.

Statement 2 is correct.  Methane's GWP is substantially higher than CO₂'s over shorter timeframes (like 20 years), making it a potent contributor to near-term warming.  Although CO₂ has a longer atmospheric lifetime, methane's initial warming effect is far more pronounced.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The overwhelming scientific consensus attributes the increase in atmospheric greenhouse gas concentrations to anthropogenic (human-caused) activities, primarily the burning of fossil fuels, deforestation, and industrial processes.  Natural processes like volcanic eruptions contribute negligibly to the overall increase in greenhouse gases compared to human activities.


**4.  Consider the following statements regarding ozone:**

1.  Stratospheric ozone plays a crucial role in absorbing harmful ultraviolet (UV) radiation from the sun.
2.  Ground-level ozone is a secondary pollutant formed through photochemical reactions involving nitrogen oxides (NOx) and volatile organic compounds (VOCs).
3.  The Montreal Protocol primarily addresses the issue of ground-level ozone pollution.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The stratospheric ozone layer acts as a shield, absorbing a significant portion of the sun's harmful UV-B radiation, which can cause skin cancer and other health problems.  This is a vital protective function for life on Earth.

Statement 2 is correct. Ground-level ozone is not directly emitted but is formed through complex chemical reactions involving NOx and VOCs in the presence of sunlight. This process is part of photochemical smog formation, and ground-level ozone is a significant air pollutant.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Montreal Protocol focuses on the phase-out of ozone-depleting substances (ODS) that harm the stratospheric ozone layer, not ground-level ozone.  Ground-level ozone is addressed through other air quality regulations and emission control measures.


**5. With reference to climate change, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change (IPCC) provides regular assessments on climate change science and impacts.
2. The Paris Agreement aims to limit global warming to well below 2°C, preferably to 1.5°C, compared to pre-industrial levels.
3.  Melting permafrost is a negative feedback mechanism that mitigates the effects of climate change.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The IPCC, a leading international body, synthesizes scientific knowledge on climate change, providing crucial assessments for policymakers and researchers.  These reports are widely considered the most authoritative source of information on climate change science.

Statement 2 is correct. The Paris Agreement, a landmark international accord, sets ambitious targets for reducing greenhouse gas emissions to limit global temperature increases.  The 1.5°C target is especially significant as exceeding it could lead to significantly more severe consequences.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Melting permafrost is a positive feedback mechanism, not a negative one.  As permafrost thaws, it releases large amounts of methane and carbon dioxide, further amplifying global warming.  This exacerbates the initial warming effect rather than mitigating it.

**1. Consider the following statements about Methane (CH₄):**

1.  Methane's 100-year global warming potential is significantly lower than that of carbon dioxide.
2.  Methanogenic archaea, found in anaerobic environments, are the primary biological source of atmospheric methane.
3.  The oxidation of methane in the atmosphere is primarily catalyzed by hydroxyl radicals (OH).

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct. Methanogens, a type of archaea, are microorganisms that produce methane as a byproduct of their metabolism.  They thrive in anaerobic (oxygen-deficient) environments like wetlands, rice paddies, and the digestive tracts of ruminant animals.  These environments provide the necessary conditions for methanogenesis, making methanogens the primary biological source of atmospheric methane.

Statement 3 is also correct. Hydroxyl radicals (OH) are highly reactive molecules in the atmosphere that act as the primary sink for methane.  They initiate a chain of chemical reactions that ultimately lead to the oxidation of methane into carbon dioxide and water vapor. This process is crucial for regulating atmospheric methane concentrations.

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While methane has a shorter atmospheric lifetime than carbon dioxide, its global warming potential (GWP) over a 100-year period is significantly *higher* than that of CO2.  The GWP of methane is often cited as being around 25 times that of CO2 over a 100-year timeframe. This means that a given mass of methane traps substantially more heat in the atmosphere than an equivalent mass of CO2 over this period.  The 20-year GWP is even higher, reflecting methane's more rapid warming impact over shorter timescales.  The statement misrepresents the relative warming potential of methane and carbon dioxide.


**2. With reference to the impact of global warming on the Indian monsoon, consider the following statements:**

1.  Increased temperatures lead to a more predictable and consistent monsoon pattern, reducing variability.
2.  The rise in sea surface temperatures in the Indian Ocean significantly influences monsoon intensity and rainfall distribution.
3.  Deforestation in the Himalayan region has a negligible effect on regional monsoon patterns.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct.  Sea surface temperatures (SSTs) in the Indian Ocean are a key driver of the Indian monsoon system.  Global warming leads to increased SSTs, which in turn can alter the intensity, duration, and spatial distribution of monsoon rainfall.  Warmer SSTs can lead to stronger monsoons in some areas and weaker monsoons in others, resulting in increased variability and potential for both droughts and floods.  The complex interplay between SSTs and atmospheric circulation patterns is a critical factor in understanding the impact of climate change on the Indian monsoon.

Statement 1 is incorrect. Global warming, and the associated changes in atmospheric and oceanic circulation, actually lead to a *less* predictable and *more* variable monsoon pattern.  Increased frequency of extreme weather events like prolonged droughts in some regions and intense rainfall leading to floods in others is observed. The onset, intensity, and duration of the monsoon are becoming less predictable, posing significant challenges to agriculture and water resource management in India.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Deforestation in the Himalayan region significantly impacts regional monsoon patterns. The Himalayas play a crucial role in influencing monsoon circulation.  Deforestation reduces evapotranspiration, alters atmospheric moisture content, and can disrupt regional wind patterns, all of which can affect the distribution and amount of monsoon rainfall.  This effect is particularly noticeable in the regions immediately adjacent to the Himalayas.


**3. Consider the following statements regarding ozone depletion:**

1.  The Antarctic ozone hole is primarily a springtime phenomenon due to the unique interaction of polar stratospheric clouds and ozone-depleting substances within the polar vortex.
2.  Methane (CH₄) is a significant ozone-depleting substance in the stratosphere, comparable in impact to chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs).
3.  Tropospheric ozone is beneficial to human health and the environment.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 accurately describes the formation of the Antarctic ozone hole.  The polar vortex, a strong, circumpolar wind pattern, isolates cold air over Antarctica during winter.  This cold air allows for the formation of polar stratospheric clouds (PSCs), which provide surfaces for chemical reactions involving ozone-depleting substances like CFCs.  When sunlight returns in spring, these reactions are accelerated, leading to a rapid depletion of ozone. This seasonal pattern is unique to the polar regions and is a key feature distinguishing the Antarctic ozone hole.


Statement 2 is incorrect. While methane is a greenhouse gas, it is not a significant ozone-depleting substance in the stratosphere.  The primary ozone-depleting substances are halocarbons, including CFCs, which contain chlorine or bromine atoms that catalytically destroy ozone molecules. Methane does not contain these halogen atoms.


Statement 3 is incorrect.  Tropospheric ozone, unlike stratospheric ozone, is a harmful air pollutant.  It is a major component of smog and has significant negative impacts on human health, causing respiratory problems and other health issues.  It also damages crops and other vegetation.  Therefore, tropospheric ozone is detrimental to both human health and the environment.


**4. With reference to the sources of methane emissions, consider the following statements:**

1.  Enteric fermentation in livestock is a major source of methane emissions, primarily from cow belching.
2.  Rice paddies release significant amounts of methane due to anaerobic decomposition of organic matter in flooded soils.
3.  Landfills are a negligible source of methane emissions compared to agricultural sources.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Enteric fermentation, the digestive process in ruminant animals (like cows, sheep, and goats), produces significant amounts of methane as a byproduct.  This methane is released primarily through belching (eructation), rather than flatulence.  The large global population of livestock contributes substantially to global methane emissions.


Statement 2 is correct.  Rice paddies are significant sources of methane emissions. The flooded conditions in rice fields create anaerobic environments, promoting the activity of methanogenic microorganisms that decompose organic matter and release methane.  This makes rice cultivation a considerable contributor to global methane emissions.


Statement 3 is incorrect. Landfills are a substantial source of methane emissions.  The anaerobic decomposition of organic waste in landfills generates large quantities of methane. This makes landfills significant contributors to anthropogenic methane emissions, comparable to or even exceeding emissions from some agricultural sources depending on the region and management practices.  The statement significantly underestimates the contribution of landfills to global methane emissions.


**5. Consider the following statements about the Himalayan region:**

1.  The Himalayas are geologically stable and have reached isostatic equilibrium.
2.  The Himalayas significantly influence the climate of the Indian subcontinent by acting as a barrier to the monsoon winds.
3.  The Himalayas are primarily composed of igneous rocks.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b) 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct. The Himalayas play a crucial role in shaping the climate of the Indian subcontinent. Their towering height acts as a barrier, influencing the path and intensity of monsoon winds.  The mountains force the moisture-laden monsoon winds to rise, leading to orographic precipitation (rain and snow) on the windward slopes.  This orographic effect is responsible for the high rainfall in many parts of the Indian subcontinent, particularly in the northern and northeastern regions.  The Himalayas also block cold winds from Central Asia, further influencing the temperature and precipitation patterns in the region.

Statement 1 is incorrect. The Himalayas are geologically *active* and are still undergoing uplift due to the ongoing collision between the Indian and Eurasian tectonic plates.  They have not yet reached isostatic equilibrium, a state of balance between the weight of the mountains and the buoyant force of the underlying mantle.  The ongoing tectonic activity makes the Himalayas prone to earthquakes and landslides.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Himalayas are primarily composed of sedimentary and metamorphic rocks, formed from the accumulation and transformation of sediments in the ancient Tethys Ocean.  While igneous rocks may be present in some areas, they are not the dominant rock type in the Himalayan range.  The complex geological history of the Himalayas involves the collision of tectonic plates, leading to the formation of folded and faulted sedimentary and metamorphic rocks.

**1. Consider the following statements regarding the greenhouse effect:**

1.  Subtropical areas experience an enhanced greenhouse effect due to higher solar radiation and lower atmospheric humidity.
2.  The greenhouse effect is primarily caused by the absorption of outgoing longwave radiation by greenhouse gases like carbon dioxide and water vapor.
3.  Small particles of water, while contributing to atmospheric humidity, have a negligible direct impact on the greenhouse effect compared to greenhouse gases.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Subtropical regions receive higher solar radiation than temperate or polar regions, leading to increased surface temperatures. Lower atmospheric humidity in these areas allows for less efficient radiative cooling, exacerbating the greenhouse effect.  The concentration of greenhouse gases is also often higher in subtropical areas, further amplifying the warming effect.

Statement 2 is also correct. The greenhouse effect is fundamentally driven by the absorption of outgoing longwave infrared radiation (heat) emitted by the Earth's surface.  Greenhouse gases, such as carbon dioxide, methane, nitrous oxide, and water vapor, are particularly effective at absorbing these wavelengths, trapping heat within the atmosphere. This process is crucial for maintaining habitable temperatures on Earth, but an increase in greenhouse gas concentrations intensifies the effect, leading to global warming.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While small particles of water (aerosols) can influence the Earth's radiative balance through scattering and absorption of incoming solar radiation, their direct contribution to the greenhouse effect is minimal compared to the effect of greenhouse gases. The greenhouse effect primarily depends on the ability of gases to absorb and re-emit longwave radiation, a property that water aerosols don't possess to a significant degree.  While water vapor is a potent greenhouse gas, the statement focuses on the *direct* effect of small water *particles*, which is significantly different.


**2. With reference to the impact of global warming, consider the following statements:**

1.  Global warming directly causes ozone depletion in the stratosphere.
2.  Global warming increases the frequency of severe cyclones in the north Indian Ocean by altering ocean temperatures and atmospheric circulation patterns.
3.  Global warming shifts the distribution and formation patterns of sun-blocking clouds, potentially leading to amplified warming in some regions.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c) 2 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Global warming and ozone depletion are distinct but related environmental issues.  While both involve changes in atmospheric composition, they are caused by different mechanisms.  Ozone depletion is primarily caused by the release of ozone-depleting substances (ODS) like chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs), while global warming is primarily caused by increased greenhouse gas concentrations.  Although there can be indirect interactions, there is no direct causal link where global warming directly causes ozone depletion.

Statement 2 is correct.  Warming ocean surface temperatures provide more energy to the atmosphere, fueling the intensification and increased frequency of tropical cyclones. Changes in atmospheric circulation patterns, driven by global warming, also influence the track, intensity, and formation locations of these storms.  The north Indian Ocean is particularly vulnerable to these changes.

Statement 3 is correct. Global warming can alter cloud formation patterns.  Changes in atmospheric temperature and humidity influence the types and distribution of clouds.  Some cloud types, such as certain high-altitude clouds, can have a warming effect, while others, such as low-altitude clouds, can have a cooling effect.  A shift towards more warming-type clouds or a reduction in cooling clouds would lead to amplified warming in certain regions.


**3. With reference to the sources of greenhouse gases, consider the following statements:**

1.  Rice cultivation is a significant source of methane emissions due to anaerobic decomposition of organic matter in flooded paddy fields.
2.  The burning of sugarcane residue releases predominantly carbon dioxide, with minimal methane emissions.
3.  Nitrous oxide (N2O) emissions are primarily attributed to the use of nitrogen-based fertilizers in agriculture.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 3 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Flooded rice paddies create anaerobic conditions in the soil, promoting the activity of methanogenic microorganisms that produce methane (CH4) as a byproduct of organic matter decomposition. This makes rice cultivation a significant source of anthropogenic methane emissions.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While burning sugarcane residue does release carbon dioxide (CO2), it also significantly contributes to methane emissions. The incomplete combustion of organic matter in the burning process generates methane along with other greenhouse gases. The statement underestimates the methane contribution.

Statement 3 is correct. Nitrous oxide (N2O) is a potent greenhouse gas, and a significant portion of its emissions originates from agricultural practices. The use of nitrogen-based fertilizers, especially urea, leads to the release of N2O through microbial processes in the soil.  This highlights the environmental impact of intensive agricultural practices.


**4. Consider the following statements concerning the greenhouse effect and its impact:**

1.  The natural greenhouse effect maintains the average global temperature at approximately 15°C, making life on Earth possible.
2.  Without the greenhouse effect, the average global temperature would be significantly lower, around -17°C, rendering the planet uninhabitable.
3.  The enhanced greenhouse effect, caused by human activities, leads to an increase in atmospheric aerosols, thus mitigating the impact of increased greenhouse gases.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The natural greenhouse effect, a natural process involving the trapping of heat by atmospheric gases, is essential for maintaining a habitable temperature on Earth.  Without this effect, the planet would be significantly colder, making the existence of life as we know it impossible.

Statement 2 is correct. Scientific evidence strongly supports the assertion that without the natural greenhouse effect, the Earth's average temperature would be drastically lower, approximately -17°C. This is because greenhouse gases trap outgoing longwave radiation, preventing significant heat loss to space.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While human activities do increase atmospheric aerosols, these aerosols have a complex and often indirect effect on the greenhouse effect. Some aerosols can have a cooling effect by reflecting incoming solar radiation, but others can have a warming effect.  The statement incorrectly suggests that increased aerosols mitigate the warming impact of greenhouse gases; the relationship is far more nuanced and not uniformly mitigating.  The enhanced greenhouse effect is primarily driven by increased greenhouse gas concentrations, not a balance with aerosols.


**5.  With reference to the chemical composition of the atmosphere and its role in climate change, consider the following statements:**

1.  Water vapor is the most abundant greenhouse gas in the atmosphere,  constituting a variable percentage of the total atmospheric volume depending on climate and altitude.
2.  Methane (CH4) has a much shorter atmospheric lifetime than carbon dioxide (CO2), but a higher global warming potential over a 20-year period.
3.  Carbon monoxide (CO) is a significant greenhouse gas directly contributing to global warming.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (a) 1 and 2 only

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Water vapor is indeed the most abundant greenhouse gas, but its atmospheric concentration is highly variable, depending on factors such as temperature, humidity, and altitude.  It plays a crucial role in the Earth's climate system through its influence on radiative transfer and cloud formation.

Statement 2 is correct. Methane has a much shorter atmospheric lifetime compared to carbon dioxide, meaning it breaks down faster. However, its global warming potential (GWP) is significantly higher over shorter timeframes (e.g., 20 years). This means that although methane doesn't persist as long, it traps considerably more heat during its time in the atmosphere.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Carbon monoxide (CO) is not a significant greenhouse gas. While it is a pollutant with various adverse effects on human health and the environment, it does not effectively absorb and re-emit longwave radiation like the major greenhouse gases (CO2, CH4, N2O, etc.). Its primary impact on climate change is indirect, through its influence on other atmospheric processes.

**1. Consider the following statements about Jharkhand's geographical features:**

1. The Subarnarekha River, originating in Jharkhand, flows through the state before draining into the Bay of Bengal.
2. Jharkhand contains significant reserves of bauxite, a key aluminum ore.
3. The Chotanagpur Plateau, a prominent geological formation, entirely encompasses Jharkhand's geographical area.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Subarnarekha River does indeed originate in Jharkhand and flows through a significant portion of the state before emptying into the Bay of Bengal.  This is a well-established geographical fact.

Statement 2 is also correct. Jharkhand possesses substantial bauxite reserves, making it a significant producer of the ore. This is a key aspect of Jharkhand's mineral wealth and its contribution to India's aluminum industry.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Chotanagpur Plateau is a significant geological feature that covers a large part of Jharkhand, it does *not* entirely encompass the state's geographical area.  Parts of Jharkhand fall outside the boundaries of the plateau.  This is a crucial distinction that requires precise geographical knowledge.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are therefore incorrect because they either incorrectly include or exclude one or more of these statements.  Understanding the precise extent of the Chotanagpur Plateau within Jharkhand's boundaries is vital for accurate geographical analysis.

**4. With reference to the impact of climate change on India, consider the following statements:**

1. The increasing frequency and intensity of cyclones in the Bay of Bengal are primarily attributed to the rise in global average temperatures.
2.  The 2018 Kerala floods were significantly influenced by unusually heavy rainfall patterns linked to anthropogenic climate change.
3. The melting of Himalayan glaciers is solely caused by localized pollution and deforestation.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The warming of the Bay of Bengal's waters, a direct consequence of global warming, is a major factor contributing to the increased frequency and intensity of cyclones in the region. This showcases an understanding of climate change's impact on weather patterns.

Statement 2 is also correct. The 2018 Kerala floods were indeed exacerbated by unusually high rainfall, which can be linked to the larger trends of anthropogenic climate change and its impact on monsoon patterns.  This demonstrates an ability to connect specific events to broader climate change trends.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While localized pollution and deforestation contribute to changes in regional monsoon patterns, the melting of Himalayan glaciers is a complex process primarily driven by rising global temperatures, a consequence of greenhouse gas emissions. This illustrates the need to understand the multifaceted nature of climate change's impact and avoid oversimplification. Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they fail to accurately assess the primary drivers of the increased cyclone activity in the Bay of Bengal and the melting of Himalayan glaciers. This question assesses the ability to differentiate between global and local factors affecting climate change impacts.


**5. Consider the following statements regarding greenhouse gases:**

1.  Methane (CH4) has a higher global warming potential than carbon dioxide (CO2) over a 20-year period.
2. Nitrous oxide (N2O) has a significantly longer atmospheric lifetime than methane (CH4).
3. Carbon monoxide (CO) is a major contributor to ozone depletion in the stratosphere.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Methane's global warming potential is considerably higher than CO2's over shorter timeframes (like 20 years), making it a more potent greenhouse gas in the short term.

Statement 2 is correct. N2O persists in the atmosphere for a much longer duration than methane, contributing to long-term climate change effects.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While carbon monoxide is a pollutant, it is not a major contributor to stratospheric ozone depletion.  That role is primarily played by chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs) and other ozone-depleting substances.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are therefore incorrect due to the misattribution of ozone depletion to carbon monoxide. The question tests the understanding of the relative potency and atmospheric lifetime of various greenhouse gases, requiring specific knowledge about their properties.


**6. With reference to air pollution and its health impacts, consider the following statements:**

1. Exposure to benzene pollution is primarily linked to automobile exhaust, tobacco smoke, and industrial emissions.
2.  Sulphur dioxide (SO2) emissions contribute significantly to acid rain and respiratory health problems.
3.  Ammonia (NH3) released from agricultural fertilizers primarily contributes to stratospheric ozone depletion.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Benzene is a major component of automobile exhaust and tobacco smoke, and is also released during industrial processes.

Statement 2 is correct.  SO2 is a significant contributor to acid rain and causes various respiratory illnesses.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While ammonia is a pollutant, its primary contribution to environmental problems is through the formation of secondary particulate matter and eutrophication of water bodies, not stratospheric ozone depletion.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they incorrectly assess the role of ammonia in ozone depletion.  This question tests the knowledge of specific air pollutants, their sources, and their various health and environmental impacts.  The ability to differentiate between the effects of different pollutants is crucial.


**7. With reference to the consequences of global warming, consider the following statements:**

1. Ocean deoxygenation, the expansion of oxygen minimum zones (OMZs), is primarily caused by increased water temperatures due to global warming.
2.  The "social cost of carbon" is a monetary measure of the long-term economic damages caused by emitting one ton of CO2 into the atmosphere.
3.  Carbon fertilization, the increased plant growth due to rising atmospheric CO2, is a universally beneficial effect of increased CO2 concentrations.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Warmer ocean temperatures reduce oxygen solubility and contribute to stratification, leading to the expansion of OMZs.

Statement 2 is correct. The social cost of carbon accurately reflects the economic losses associated with CO2 emissions.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While carbon fertilization can increase plant growth in the short term, it is not universally beneficial due to the overall negative effects of climate change.  Options (b), (c), and (d) are therefore incorrect because they misrepresent the short-term benefits and long-term consequences of carbon fertilization. This question tests understanding of complex climate change consequences, requiring nuanced knowledge of various impacts and their interconnectedness.  The ability to distinguish between short-term and long-term effects is essential.


**8.  With reference to the Antarctic ozone hole, consider the following statements:**

1. The formation of the Antarctic ozone hole is primarily due to the presence of a strong polar vortex and the formation of Polar Stratospheric Clouds (PSCs).
2.  Chlorine atoms, released from the photodissociation of ozone-depleting substances (ODS) like CFCs, are the primary catalysts in ozone destruction.
3.  The Arctic region experiences a larger and more persistent ozone hole than the Antarctic region due to higher temperatures.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The strong polar vortex and PSCs in the Antarctic create conditions conducive to ozone depletion.

Statement 2 is correct. Chlorine atoms released from ODS are the key drivers of ozone destruction in the Antarctic.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The Antarctic ozone hole is larger and more persistent than the Arctic ozone hole due to the much stronger and longer-lasting polar vortex and colder temperatures in the Antarctic. Options (b), (c), and (d) are thus incorrect because they fail to accurately describe the relative sizes and persistence of the ozone holes in the Arctic and Antarctic regions.  This question assesses detailed knowledge of the chemical processes and atmospheric dynamics involved in ozone depletion.


**9. Consider the following statements about the impact of nanoparticles (NPs) on the ozone layer:**

1. Hydroxyl radicals (OH) are the primary oxidants responsible for removing ozone-depleting substances in the stratosphere.
2.  Nanoparticles (NPs) enhance the breakdown of ozone-depleting substances by increasing the concentration of hydroxyl radicals (OH).
3.  The Montreal Protocol primarily addresses the issue of ozone depletion by regulating the production and consumption of ozone-depleting substances.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. OH radicals play a crucial role in removing ODS from the stratosphere.

Statement 2 is incorrect. NPs, due to their high reactivity, actually *reduce* the concentration of OH radicals, hindering the breakdown of ODS and thus prolonging their presence in the atmosphere.

Statement 3 is correct. The Montreal Protocol is the international treaty designed to protect the ozone layer by phasing out ODS. Options (b), (c), and (d) are therefore incorrect due to the inaccurate description of the impact of nanoparticles on hydroxyl radicals. This question tests the understanding of the complex interactions between nanoparticles, hydroxyl radicals, and ozone-depleting substances in the stratosphere.  It requires a precise understanding of the chemical processes involved.


**10. With reference to the geographical distribution of various tribes in India, consider the following statements:**

1. The Munda tribe inhabits Jharkhand and Odisha.
2. The Santhal tribe is predominantly found in Jharkhand, Odisha and Bihar.
3. The Bhumij tribe is exclusively found in Jharkhand.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Munda tribe has a significant presence in both Jharkhand and Odisha, demonstrating knowledge of tribal distribution across states.

Statement 2 is correct. The Santhal tribe is indeed found across Jharkhand, Odisha, and Bihar. This shows understanding of the wider geographical spread of some tribal groups.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While the Bhumij tribe has a strong presence in Jharkhand,  it's also found in other states, illustrating the need for precise knowledge of tribal distribution. Options (b), (c), and (d) are therefore incorrect because they fail to accurately represent the distribution of the Bhumij tribe across states. This question tests specific knowledge of tribal groups and their geographical distribution across various Indian states, highlighting the complexity and diversity of India's tribal populations.

**1. With reference to the Environment (Protection) Act, 1986, consider the following statements:**

1. The Act explicitly defines Eco-Sensitive Zones (ESZs) and mandates their establishment around protected areas.
2. The Central Ground Water Board is a body constituted under the Environment (Protection) Act, 1986, responsible for groundwater management.
3. The Act empowers the Central Government to set standards for emission and discharge of environmental pollutants.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 3 is correct. The Environment (Protection) Act, 1986, provides the Central Government with broad powers to regulate environmental pollution. This includes setting standards for emission and discharge of pollutants from various sources.  The Act's wide-ranging authority allows it to address diverse environmental concerns.

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While the Environment (Protection) Act, 1986, is the overarching legislation for environmental protection in India, the specific definition and establishment of Eco-Sensitive Zones (ESZs) are not directly addressed within the Act itself.  ESZs are a concept developed and implemented through subsequent notifications and guidelines issued by the Ministry of Environment, Forest and Climate Change.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The Central Ground Water Board (CGWB) is an organization under the Ministry of Jal Shakti. While its work is crucial for environmental protection, particularly concerning groundwater resources, it is not directly constituted under the Environment (Protection) Act, 1986.  The CGWA, however, *is* constituted under the EPA, 1986.  This distinction is a key point often missed in UPSC preparation.


**2. With reference to international environmental organizations, consider the following statements:**

1. The International Union for Conservation of Nature (IUCN) is responsible for designating and managing Blue Flag beaches globally.
2. The United Nations Environment Programme (UNEP) sets the price for carbon credits traded internationally.
3. The World Wide Fund for Nature (WWF) solely conducts research on the impact of sea-level rise.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are incorrect.  While the IUCN is a significant player in conservation efforts, the designation of Blue Flag beaches is handled by the Foundation for Environmental Education (FEE), an independent organization.  UNEP plays a crucial role in environmental governance, but it doesn't directly set the price of carbon credits; the price is determined by market forces within the established carbon trading mechanisms.  WWF is involved in research on sea-level rise, but it's not the sole entity conducting such research; numerous other organizations and research institutions contribute to this area of study.


**3. Consider the following statements about the Global Environment Facility (GEF):**

1. The GEF serves as the financial mechanism for the Convention on Biological Diversity (CBD) but not the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change (UNFCCC).
2. The GEF primarily funds scientific research on global environmental issues.
3. The GEF works exclusively with OECD member countries to transfer technology and funds for environmental protection.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The GEF acts as a financial mechanism for both the CBD and the UNFCCC, along with other international environmental conventions.  It plays a vital role in providing funding for projects that address global environmental challenges.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the GEF may fund projects that involve scientific research, its primary function is not to conduct or directly fund scientific research itself.  Its focus is on providing financial and technical support for implementing environmental projects.  Research is often a component of these projects but not the GEF's core mandate.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The GEF works with a diverse range of countries, not limiting its collaborations to only OECD member countries. Its mandate includes supporting developing countries in their efforts to protect their environments and achieve sustainable development.


**4. With reference to the Ministry of Housing and Urban Affairs (MoHUA), consider the following statements:**

1. The MoHUA directly funds and manages the India Sanitation Coalition.
2. The National Institute of Urban Affairs (NIUA) is an autonomous body under the MoHUA.
3. The MoHUA is solely responsible for dealing with all aspects of Urban Local Government in India.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 is correct. The NIUA is indeed an apex body under the MoHUA, playing a crucial role in providing innovative solutions for urban challenges.

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While the MoHUA is heavily involved in sanitation initiatives, the India Sanitation Coalition is a collaborative platform involving multiple stakeholders, including government agencies, NGOs, and international organizations. The MoHUA's role is part of a larger network of contributors.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While the MoHUA is the primary ministry dealing with urban governance, other ministries and departments also have relevant roles and responsibilities related to urban development and local governments.  There are often overlapping jurisdictions and collaborations with other government bodies.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. With reference to the New York Declaration on Forests, consider the following statements:**

1. The declaration primarily focuses on halting deforestation by 2020, with a secondary emphasis on forest restoration.
2.  The Bonn Challenge, an initiative to restore degraded and deforested lands, was significantly expanded through the commitments made in the New York Declaration.
3.  The New York Declaration is a legally binding international treaty, enforceable through international courts.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the New York Declaration on Forests aimed to reduce deforestation and forest degradation, the target year was not specifically 2020. The declaration set a broader goal to halt deforestation and forest degradation by 2030 and to restore significant areas of forest by the same year. The emphasis was on both halting loss and promoting restoration.

Statement 2 is correct. The New York Declaration played a crucial role in significantly expanding the Bonn Challenge, a global effort to restore 350 million hectares of the world's degraded and deforested landscapes by 2030.  The Declaration spurred increased commitments and pledges to this initiative.

Statement 3 is incorrect. The New York Declaration on Forests is not a legally binding international treaty. It's a political declaration, a voluntary commitment by governments, businesses, and civil society organizations to achieve specific targets related to forests.  It lacks the enforcement mechanisms of a formal treaty.  The lack of legal binding is a key weakness often criticized regarding its effectiveness.  The declaration relies on the collective will and individual actions of its signatories.


**2. With reference to the UNEP's activities, consider the following statements:**

1. The UNEP directly manages and funds all projects related to the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) concerning environmental issues.
2. The UNEP publishes the Emissions Gap Report (EGR), which assesses the difference between projected greenhouse gas emissions and levels needed to meet climate targets.
3. The Climate and Clean Air Coalition (CCAC), a collaborative initiative focused on reducing short-lived climate pollutants, is not affiliated with the UNEP.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  While the UNEP plays a significant role in advocating for and supporting the achievement of SDGs related to the environment, it doesn't directly manage *all* projects.  Many initiatives are implemented by other UN agencies, national governments, and NGOs, with the UNEP often providing guidance, technical assistance, or coordination.  Funding also comes from various sources, not solely the UNEP budget.

Statement 2 is correct. The UNEP is indeed the publisher of the Emissions Gap Report (EGR), a crucial document that highlights the gap between current commitments to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and what's needed to limit global warming to agreed-upon levels.  The report's findings are vital for informing climate policy and action.
