Statement 1 is incorrect. Urea is *not* included in the NBS scheme; it remains under price control, unlike other fertilizers. This price control is a significant factor contributing to the imbalance in fertilizer use.

Statement 2 is correct. The NBS scheme's decontrolled pricing of non-urea fertilizers, coupled with urea's price control, has resulted in farmers using more urea than other nutrients, exacerbating the fertilizer imbalance.

Statement 3 is correct.  Excessive nitrogen fertilizer use leads to increased nitrous oxide (N2O) emissions, a potent greenhouse gas with a far greater global warming potential than carbon dioxide.  It also contributes to soil degradation and acidification.


These questions demonstrate the desired difficulty level and incorporate plausible distractors, forcing candidates to rely on a solid understanding of the concepts and facts.  They also require careful analysis and evaluation to determine the correct answer.

**1. With reference to ecosystem components and interactions, consider the following statements:**

1.  Mycorrhizal fungi, a type of biofertilizer, primarily enhance plant growth by producing growth-promoting hormones.
2.  The bioremediation process utilizes both bacteria and fungi to degrade pollutants like polyethylene.
3.  Sewage water, containing a variety of bacteria, undergoes bioventing to stimulate the growth of specific beneficial bacteria strains.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct. Mycorrhizal fungi are indeed a type of biofertilizer and they do enhance plant growth. However, while they can produce some growth-promoting substances, their primary mechanism is improving nutrient uptake by the plant roots through symbiotic relationships, not solely hormone production.  Therefore, the statement oversimplifies their role.

Statement 2 is correct. Bioremediation, a process designed to remove pollutants from the environment, frequently employs both bacteria and fungi due to their diverse metabolic capabilities.  These microorganisms can break down a wide range of organic and some inorganic pollutants, including polyethylene, a persistent plastic.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Bioventing is an in-situ bioremediation technique that focuses on stimulating the growth of *indigenous* (naturally present) aerobic microorganisms in soil or groundwater to break down contaminants. It doesn't specifically aim to increase the overall bacterial population in sewage water; rather, it aims to enhance the activity of existing beneficial bacteria to degrade specific pollutants.  The process doesn't simply increase the population of any bacteria; it enhances the activity of those capable of biodegrading the target pollutants.



**2. With reference to the characteristics of different ecosystems, consider the following statements:**

1.  Grassland ecosystems are characterized by rainfall between 25-75 cm annually, preventing the establishment of forests but exceeding that of true deserts.
2.  The "lungs of the planet," the Amazon rainforest, is primarily threatened by conversion to grasslands for beef cattle ranching and soybean cultivation.
3.  Shola forests, located in the Western Ghats, are primarily threatened by invasive species such as eucalyptus and acacia, but are also impacted by reduced frost due to climate change, allowing acacia expansion into grasslands.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 accurately describes the climatic conditions defining grassland ecosystems.  The intermediate rainfall prevents the growth of forests but surpasses the aridity of deserts, leading to a unique grassland biome.

Statement 2 correctly identifies the major threats to the Amazon rainforest. Deforestation for agricultural activities, particularly soybean farming and cattle ranching, is a significant driver of habitat loss in this crucial ecosystem.  The term "lungs of the planet" reflects its vital role in global carbon cycling.

Statement 3 is also correct. Shola forests, a unique montane ecosystem, face a double threat:  invasive species outcompete native vegetation, and climate change reduces frost, which historically limited the expansion of acacia and other invasive species into grasslands. This altered vegetation pattern affects water resources, increases landslide risk, and negatively impacts endangered species like the Nilgiri Tahr.


**3. With reference to ecological concepts and processes, consider the following statements:**

1.  A food web, unlike a food chain, illustrates the complex network of interconnected food chains within an ecosystem, offering multiple food sources for increased survival chances.
2.  The concept of ecological homeostasis refers to the inherent ability of ecosystems to maintain a state of equilibrium through self-regulation, primarily driven by negative feedback mechanisms.
3.  In-situ conservation is a method specifically designed to protect and preserve ecosystems by maintaining them in their natural environments, contrasting with ex-situ methods.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 accurately defines a food web.  It contrasts with a food chain's linear energy flow, showcasing the intricate network of interactions, providing alternative food sources, and enhancing the resilience of species.

Statement 2 correctly explains ecological homeostasis. This crucial concept highlights the self-regulating capacity of ecosystems to maintain stability through negative feedback mechanisms, where an increase in one factor triggers a decrease in another, and vice versa, maintaining balance.

Statement 3 correctly describes in-situ conservation. This approach prioritizes protecting ecosystems within their natural settings, unlike ex-situ conservation, which involves removing species from their natural habitat for protection (e.g., zoos, botanical gardens).


**4. With reference to nitrogen fixation and biofertilizers, consider the following statements:**

1.  Nostoc, Azotobacter, and Rhizobium are all examples of free-living nitrogen-fixing bacteria, contributing significantly to atmospheric nitrogen fixation.
2.  Azolla-Anabaena symbiosis and Mycorrhizal fungi are both examples of biofertilizers used in agriculture to enhance soil fertility and plant growth.
3.  Biofertilizers, composed of microorganisms like bacteria and fungi, primarily enhance plant growth by directly converting atmospheric nitrogen into a usable form for plants.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While Nostoc and Azotobacter are free-living nitrogen-fixing bacteria, Rhizobium is a symbiotic nitrogen-fixing bacteria that lives in the root nodules of leguminous plants.  The statement incorrectly categorizes all three as free-living.

Statement 2 is correct. Azolla-Anabaena is a symbiotic association used as a biofertilizer, and mycorrhizal fungi form symbiotic relationships with plant roots, enhancing nutrient uptake. Both contribute to improved soil fertility.

Statement 3 is partially correct.  Biofertilizers do enhance plant growth, and many are based on nitrogen-fixing microorganisms. However, the statement is an oversimplification.  While nitrogen fixation is a major benefit,  biofertilizers also enhance nutrient availability through other mechanisms like improved nutrient uptake by plants, production of growth hormones, and suppression of plant pathogens.

**1. Consider the following statements regarding nitrogen's role in biological systems:**

1.  Nitrogen, a key component of amino acids and proteins, is primarily obtained by plants through direct atmospheric uptake.
2.  The burning of coal significantly enhances nitrogen availability in soil, boosting plant growth.
3.  Microorganisms play a crucial role in converting atmospheric nitrogen into forms usable by plants.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Plants cannot directly utilize atmospheric nitrogen (N2) due to its strong triple bond.  They rely on nitrogen fixation carried out by microorganisms to convert N2 into usable forms like ammonia (NH3) or nitrates (NO3-). This process is essential for plant growth as nitrogen is a crucial component of amino acids, proteins, nucleic acids (DNA and RNA), and chlorophyll.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Burning coal releases nitrogen oxides (NOx) into the atmosphere, contributing to air pollution and acid rain, but it does not directly add usable nitrogen to the soil.  In fact, combustion processes often lead to the loss of nitrogen from the soil. While coal does contain some nitrogen, the process of burning it does not make this nitrogen bioavailable to plants.

Statement 3 is correct.  Microorganisms, specifically nitrogen-fixing bacteria and cyanobacteria (blue-green algae), are the primary agents of nitrogen fixation. They convert atmospheric nitrogen into ammonia, a form that plants can readily absorb and utilize for growth.  This process is a vital part of the nitrogen cycle, ensuring a continuous supply of this essential nutrient for the biosphere.  Different groups of bacteria participate in various stages of the nitrogen cycle, including nitrification (conversion of ammonia to nitrites and nitrates) and denitrification (conversion of nitrates back to atmospheric nitrogen).


**2. With reference to biofertilizers, consider the following statements:**

1.  Azolla-Anabaena symbiosis is an example of a biofertilizer that enhances nitrogen fixation in rice paddies.
2. Mycorrhizal fungi, while beneficial to plant growth, are not considered biofertilizers due to their complex interactions.
3.  Nostoc, a cyanobacterium, is widely used as a phosphorus-solubilizing biofertilizer.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  Azolla, a water fern, forms a symbiotic relationship with the nitrogen-fixing cyanobacterium Anabaena. This association is effectively used as a biofertilizer, particularly in rice cultivation, significantly increasing nitrogen availability in flooded rice paddies.  The Azolla-Anabaena system is a sustainable and environmentally friendly way to enhance nitrogen levels in the soil.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Mycorrhizal fungi are indeed considered biofertilizers. They form symbiotic associations with plant roots, enhancing nutrient uptake (especially phosphorus), improving water absorption, and offering disease resistance.  Their role is significant in sustainable agriculture and soil health. The statement incorrectly suggests their complex interactions disqualify them as biofertilizers.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Nostoc is a nitrogen-fixing cyanobacterium, not a phosphorus-solubilizing one. While it contributes to nitrogen enrichment in the soil, it is not known for its ability to solubilize phosphorus.  Phosphorus solubilization is primarily associated with other bacterial and fungal species.


**3. With respect to the nitrogen cycle, consider the following statements:**

1.  Denitrification is a process that converts nitrates into atmospheric nitrogen, reducing nitrogen availability in the soil.
2.  Urea, a common nitrogenous fertilizer, directly contributes to atmospheric nitrogen levels upon application to soil.
3.  Ammonification is a process where organic nitrogen is converted into ammonium ions, making it accessible to plants.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Denitrification is a microbial process that converts nitrates (NO3-) to nitrogen gas (N2) and other gaseous nitrogen oxides (N2O, NO).  This process releases nitrogen back into the atmosphere, reducing its availability for plant uptake.  It's an important part of the nitrogen cycle, preventing excessive nitrogen accumulation in the soil.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Urea, when applied to soil, is first converted by microbial action into ammonia (NH3) and then further into ammonium ions (NH4+) through ammonification.  It does not directly contribute to atmospheric nitrogen levels. The nitrogen in urea ultimately becomes part of the soil nitrogen pool, which can be used by plants or lost through processes like denitrification.

Statement 3 is correct. Ammonification is a key step in the nitrogen cycle.  It involves the decomposition of organic nitrogen-containing compounds (like proteins and nucleic acids) by microorganisms, resulting in the release of ammonium ions (NH4+).  These ammonium ions are then available for uptake by plants or can be further converted to nitrites and nitrates by nitrifying bacteria.



**4. Consider the following statements about the effects of algal blooms:**

1. Algal blooms always result in harmful effects on aquatic ecosystems.
2. Oxygen depletion during algal blooms is primarily caused by the increased respiration of phytoplankton at night.
3. The decomposition of dead algae following an algal bloom further exacerbates oxygen depletion.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While many algal blooms are harmful, some are not.  The harmfulness depends on the species of algae involved and the extent of the bloom. Some algal blooms can be benign, while others produce toxins (harmful algal blooms or HABs) that negatively impact aquatic life and human health.

Statement 2 is correct. Phytoplankton, the primary organisms involved in algal blooms, are photosynthetic during the day, producing oxygen. However, at night, they respire, consuming oxygen.  In a large algal bloom, the high concentration of phytoplankton leads to significantly increased oxygen consumption at night, contributing to oxygen depletion.

Statement 3 is correct. When an algal bloom collapses, the massive amount of dead algae undergoes decomposition by microorganisms.  This decomposition process consumes significant amounts of oxygen, further reducing oxygen levels in the water body, often leading to hypoxic (low oxygen) or anoxic (no oxygen) conditions that can cause fish kills and damage the ecosystem.


**5. With reference to biopesticides, consider the following statements:**

1. All biopesticides are derived from naturally occurring sources without any genetic modification.
2. Bacteria and fungi are examples of microbial pesticides that offer more targeted pest control than conventional chemicals.
3. Plant-incorporated protectants (PIPs) are a type of biopesticide produced by genetically modified plants.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While many biopesticides are derived from natural sources, some are produced through genetic engineering techniques.  Plant-incorporated protectants (PIPs), for example, involve the genetic modification of plants to produce pesticidal substances.  The definition of biopesticides is broader than strictly naturally occurring substances.

Statement 2 is correct. Microbial pesticides, which include bacteria and fungi, are a significant component of biopesticides. They offer a more targeted approach to pest control compared to broad-spectrum conventional chemical pesticides.  They often act on specific pests, minimizing harm to beneficial organisms and the environment.

Statement 3 is correct. Plant-incorporated protectants (PIPs) are indeed a type of biopesticide.  They are produced by plants that have been genetically modified to express genes for pesticidal proteins or other compounds.  This technology offers a sustainable and integrated pest management approach, reducing reliance on synthetic chemical pesticides.

**27. With reference to Bacillus thuringiensis and its applications, consider the following statements:**

1.  Bt brinjal is a genetically modified crop variety that incorporates genes from Bacillus thuringiensis to enhance pest resistance, specifically targeting the brinjal fruit and shoot borer.
2.  The Bt toxin produced by Bacillus thuringiensis is a protein that acts as an insecticide, primarily affecting the larval stages of specific insect species.  Bt cotton, a widely cultivated GM crop, utilizes this mechanism.
3.  Bacillus thuringiensis is a bacterium used exclusively in the production of genetically modified crops, with no other significant applications in agriculture or pest control.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is largely correct. Bt brinjal is indeed a genetically modified (GM) crop engineered to express genes from *Bacillus thuringiensis*, leading to increased resistance against the brinjal fruit and shoot borer.  However, the statement slightly oversimplifies the mechanism; the Bt toxin affects a range of insect pests and isn't limited solely to the mentioned borer.

Statement 2 is accurate. *Bacillus thuringiensis* produces a crystalline protein, often called Bt toxin, which acts as a potent insecticide. This toxin is effective against the larval stages of many insects. Bt cotton is a prime example of a GM crop successfully utilizing this protein for pest control. The statement correctly identifies the insecticidal nature of the toxin and its application in Bt cotton.

Statement 3 is incorrect. While *Bacillus thuringiensis* is extensively used in GM crop production, it's inaccurate to say it's *exclusively* used in this context.  It's also a commonly employed microbial biopesticide, directly applied as a spray to control various insect pests in conventional agriculture.  Its application isn't limited to GM crops.  Therefore, this statement presents a significant oversimplification and is factually inaccurate.

Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they fail to accurately reflect the true nature of Bacillus thuringiensis's applications. Option (c) is the only option that correctly identifies the accurate statements 1 and 2, while recognizing the inaccuracy of statement 3.  The question tests the candidate's knowledge of Bt technology and its broader applications beyond just GM crops, highlighting the need for nuanced understanding of the subject.


**28. With reference to the concept of ecosystem services, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Millennium Ecosystem Assessment (MEA), a UN-sponsored initiative, categorized ecosystem services into provisioning, regulating, cultural, and supporting services;  photosynthesis is a key regulating service.
2.  Nutrient cycling, a supporting ecosystem service, is crucial for maintaining the productivity and functioning of ecosystems; its disruption can significantly impact food production.
3.  Upwelling, an oceanic process that brings nutrient-rich water to the surface, is primarily a cultural ecosystem service, enhancing recreational activities and tourism.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is partially correct. The MEA did indeed categorize ecosystem services as described. However, photosynthesis is a *supporting* service, not a regulating service.  Regulating services involve the control of ecosystem processes, such as climate regulation or disease control, while supporting services are fundamental processes necessary for the production of all other ecosystem services. Photosynthesis is foundational, providing the base for energy flow in most ecosystems.

Statement 2 is correct. Nutrient cycling is indeed a supporting ecosystem service.  The cycling of essential nutrients like nitrogen and phosphorus is vital for maintaining ecosystem health and productivity.  Disruptions to nutrient cycles (e.g., through pollution or deforestation) can have severe consequences on agricultural yields and overall food security.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Upwelling is a crucial *supporting* ecosystem service, not a cultural one. While upwelling might indirectly support cultural services (e.g., by increasing fish populations that are then harvested or observed), its primary function is to bring nutrient-rich waters to the surface, boosting primary productivity and supporting the entire marine food web.  Cultural services relate to non-material benefits people obtain from ecosystems.

Options (a), (b), and (d) are incorrect because they misclassify the types of ecosystem services involved. Option (c) is correct because it accurately identifies statements 1 (with the correction regarding photosynthesis's classification) and 2 as correct while recognizing the misclassification in statement 3. The question tests understanding of the MEA framework and the different categories of ecosystem services, requiring careful distinction between supporting and regulating roles.



**29. Consider the following statements regarding keystone species and their ecological roles:**

1.  Keystone species, such as the tiger or elephant, exert disproportionate influence on their ecosystems, maintaining biodiversity and ecosystem structure even if they are not the most abundant species.
2.  The removal of a keystone species always leads to a complete collapse of the ecosystem and the extinction of many other species.
3.  The concept of a keystone species was introduced by Robert T. Paine, highlighting the significant impact of certain species on community structure, regardless of their abundance.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. Keystone species, by definition, have a disproportionately large effect on their environment relative to their abundance.  Tigers and elephants are often cited examples, where their presence or absence dramatically alters the composition and dynamics of their respective ecosystems.  Their impact is out of proportion to their numbers.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the removal of a keystone species can cause significant disruptions to an ecosystem, it does not always lead to complete collapse or the extinction of numerous other species.  The impact varies depending on the specific ecosystem and the role of the keystone species.  Ecosystems exhibit resilience and are capable of adapting to some degree, even in the absence of a keystone species.

Statement 3 is correct.  Robert T. Paine is correctly credited with introducing the concept of keystone species in his influential work, emphasizing that certain species play crucial roles in maintaining community structure and diversity, even if their populations are relatively small.

Options (b), (c), and (d) are incorrect because they either misrepresent the ecological consequences of keystone species removal or incorrectly attribute the origin of the concept. Option (a) accurately identifies statements 1 and 3 as being correct, while acknowledging the inaccuracy of statement 2, thereby demonstrating a precise understanding of the concept of keystone species and its implications.  The question tests knowledge of ecological concepts and the ability to differentiate between extreme and nuanced interpretations of ecological phenomena.

**1. With reference to keystone species, consider the following statements:**

1.  Elephants, due to their significant impact on vegetation and water sources, are considered keystone species in several African savanna ecosystems.  Their role extends to influencing the distribution and abundance of other herbivores.
2.  Corals, while not apex predators, are keystone species in coral reef ecosystems. Their presence structures the habitat and supports a vast array of other species, impacting the overall biodiversity.
3.  Pollinators, including various insects and birds, are crucial keystone species globally, impacting plant reproduction and consequently impacting food webs and overall ecosystem stability.  Their decline significantly affects biodiversity.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect the role of different organisms as keystone species.  Statement 1 correctly identifies elephants as keystone species in certain ecosystems, highlighting their influence on vegetation and other herbivores. Their large size and feeding habits create significant changes in their environment, impacting a wide range of species.  Statement 2 accurately points out the crucial role of corals as keystone species in coral reef ecosystems.  While not predators in the traditional sense, their presence provides the physical structure of the reef, creating habitat for countless other organisms. The loss of corals leads to a catastrophic collapse of the ecosystem. Statement 3 correctly identifies pollinators as keystone species, emphasizing their vital role in plant reproduction and the consequent impact on food webs.  Their decline directly threatens plant diversity and ecosystem stability.  Therefore, all three statements are true and accurately describe examples of keystone species and their ecological importance.


**2. With reference to the impact of DDT on ecosystems, consider the following statements:**

1.  DDT, being a persistent organic pollutant, primarily accumulates in the fatty tissues of organisms at lower trophic levels, with minimal biomagnification effects.
2.  Biomagnification of DDT results in higher concentrations of the pesticide in apex predators, leading to reproductive issues and neurological damage.  Eagles are a well-known example of this phenomenon.
3. Dicofol, a pesticide chemically related to DDT, exhibits similar bioaccumulation and biomagnification patterns, posing comparable threats to wildlife.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  DDT, due to its persistence and lipid solubility, does indeed accumulate in organisms, but it is crucially *not* limited to lower trophic levels. The core issue is biomagnification—the increasing concentration of DDT as you move up the food chain. Statement 2 is correct. Biomagnification is the key concern with DDT.  Apex predators, having consumed organisms at lower trophic levels that have accumulated DDT, experience significantly higher concentrations, leading to the detrimental effects mentioned. Eagles are a classic example, suffering from eggshell thinning and reproductive failure due to DDT biomagnification. Statement 3 is also correct.  Dicofol's chemical similarity to DDT results in a similar pattern of bioaccumulation and biomagnification, posing similar risks to wildlife.  The shared chemical structure leads to similar environmental behavior. Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are correct.


**3. With reference to sustainable agricultural practices in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  Mixed cropping, while beneficial for biodiversity and soil health, generally results in lower overall crop yields compared to monoculture farming methods.
2.  Organic manures, though environmentally friendly, often lack the nutrient density of synthetic fertilizers, potentially impacting crop productivity.
3.  The use of pest-resistant crop varieties is a key element of sustainable agriculture, reducing the need for chemical pesticides and promoting ecological balance.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Mixed cropping, or intercropping, is often associated with *higher* yields per hectare compared to monoculture due to improved resource utilization and reduced pest pressure.  While risks exist, the overall yield advantage is often reported. Statement 2 is incorrect. While synthetic fertilizers might offer higher nutrient density in the short term, organic manures contribute significantly to long-term soil health and fertility.  Their slower release of nutrients promotes sustained plant growth and reduces the risk of nutrient depletion. Statement 3 is correct.  Pest-resistant crop varieties are a cornerstone of sustainable agriculture, reducing reliance on chemical pesticides that can harm the environment and human health.  This approach promotes ecological balance by minimizing disruption to natural pest control mechanisms.  Therefore, only statement 3 is entirely accurate.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding biomagnification:**

1.  Biomagnification primarily affects aquatic ecosystems, with minimal impact on terrestrial food chains.
2.  Heavy metals, like mercury and lead, undergo biomagnification, accumulating in higher trophic levels and posing significant health risks to consumers.
3.  Bioaccumulation refers to the increase in concentration of a substance within a single organism over time, while biomagnification describes the increase in concentration across trophic levels.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. Biomagnification affects both aquatic and terrestrial food chains. While aquatic systems are often studied due to the visibility of the process in fish, the principle applies equally to land-based food webs.  Statement 2 is correct. Heavy metals are classic examples of substances that undergo biomagnification.  Their persistence and tendency to accumulate in tissues lead to increasing concentrations in organisms at higher trophic levels, posing significant risks to human and animal health. Statement 3 is correct.  This statement accurately defines the difference between bioaccumulation (within an organism) and biomagnification (across trophic levels).  Bioaccumulation is a precursor to biomagnification.  Therefore, only statements 2 and 3 are correct.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided text, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding pesticides in India:**

1. The Central Insecticides Board (CIB) primarily registers pesticides, while the Registration Committee (RC) advises on their usage.
2.  The Insecticides Act of 1968, along with a new bill, comprehensively regulates all aspects of pesticide use and registration in India, including  DRPs.
3. Endosulfan, Chlordane, Endrin, and Heptachlor are classified as pesticides by the WHO and their use in India is strictly governed by the Ministry of Agriculture.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect because the roles of the CIB and RC are reversed. The CIB advises on pesticide usage, while the RC registers them.  Statement 2 is partially incorrect. While the Insecticides Act of 1968 is a foundational piece of legislation, the description of the "new bill" and its comprehensive regulation of DRPs (presumably,  a type of pesticide)  is too vague and potentially inaccurate without further specification.  The existence of a new bill regulating pesticides doesn't automatically validate the entirety of statement 2.  Statement 3 is correct. Endosulfan, Chlordane, Endrin, and Heptachlor are indeed classified as pesticides by the WHO, and their usage in India is subject to strict regulations by the Ministry of Agriculture.  The focus on these specific chemicals highlights a factual detail that requires accurate recall, making it a suitable UPSC-style question.


**2. With reference to the impact of pesticides, consider the following statements:**

1.  Organic farming, hydroponics, and ZBNF (Zero Budget Natural Farming) techniques are all effective strategies for significantly reducing pesticide use in agriculture.
2.  The widespread use of pesticides during the Green Revolution led to a substantial increase in agricultural productivity but also caused significant harm to biodiversity and the environment.
3. The WHO's classification of pesticides considers their impact on human health (farmers), wildlife, and livestock, necessitating the use of personal protective equipment (PPE) during application.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are accurate. Statement 1 correctly identifies organic farming, hydroponics, and ZBNF as methods to reduce pesticide reliance.  Statement 2 accurately reflects the trade-offs of the Green Revolution—increased productivity at the cost of environmental and biodiversity damage. Statement 3 correctly points out the WHO's comprehensive approach to pesticide classification, considering human and environmental health risks, and the necessity of PPE. This question tests factual knowledge and the ability to synthesize information from different parts of the text.



**3. With reference to biogeochemical cycles, consider the following statements:**

1. The nitrogen cycle is a sedimentary cycle, primarily involving the movement of nitrogen between the atmosphere, biosphere, and geosphere.
2.  Photosynthesis, respiration, and the decay of organic matter are all crucial components of the carbon cycle.
3. The water cycle is a gaseous cycle that includes processes like evaporation, condensation, and precipitation, crucial for maintaining Earth's ecosystems.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect; the nitrogen cycle is a gaseous cycle, not sedimentary.  Statement 2 is correct; the listed processes are integral to the carbon cycle. Statement 3 is partially correct in describing the processes but incorrectly classifies the water cycle as gaseous. While water exists in gaseous form (water vapor) during parts of the cycle, the water cycle is more accurately described as a biogeochemical cycle involving all spheres (atmosphere, hydrosphere, lithosphere, and biosphere).  The question tests detailed knowledge of biogeochemical cycles and the ability to identify subtle inaccuracies in definitions.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding biodiversity:**

1.  The Economics of Ecosystems and Biodiversity (TEEB) initiative primarily focuses on the economic benefits of biodiversity, downplaying its ecological significance.
2.  Intensified food production practices, invasive alien species, and pollution all negatively impact biodiversity.
3.  India's Western Ghats mountain range is renowned for its exceptionally high levels of biodiversity, supporting numerous unique plant and animal species.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect; TEEB considers both economic and ecological aspects of biodiversity. Statement 2 is correct; the mentioned factors are significant threats to biodiversity. Statement 3 is also correct; the Western Ghats are globally recognized for their rich biodiversity.  This question assesses factual knowledge about biodiversity and its threats, requiring recall of specific examples and initiatives.


**5. With reference to organic farming in India, consider the following statements:**

1.  Sikkim is the first state in India to achieve 100% organic certification, followed by Lakshadweep, a Union Territory.
2.  The Paramparagat Krishi Vikas Yojana (PKVY) primarily promotes organic farming through the Participatory Guarantee System (PGS) certification, focusing on domestic markets.
3.  The Mission Organic Value Chain Development for North East Region (MOVCD-NER) emphasizes linking growers with consumers through certified organic production, targeting both domestic and export markets.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 1 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements accurately reflect facts regarding organic farming in India. Statement 1 correctly identifies Sikkim and Lakshadweep's achievements. Statement 2 accurately describes PKVY's focus. Statement 3 correctly outlines MOVCD-NER's objectives.  The question tests knowledge of specific Indian government initiatives and their goals.  The details regarding certification schemes and regional focuses are not easily recalled, increasing the question's difficulty.

**1. Consider the following statements regarding population growth in Calcutta:**

1.  The Five Year Plans explicitly aimed to mitigate the effects of Calcutta's rapid population growth on food security.
2.  The surge in Calcutta's population directly influenced the size and composition of electoral constituencies.
3.  Calcutta's population growth significantly contributed to the decline in the Total Fertility Rate (TFR) during the mid-20th century.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While the Five Year Plans addressed issues related to food security, they did not explicitly target Calcutta's population growth as the primary driver. Food security was a broader national concern influenced by multiple factors like agricultural production, distribution, and overall economic development.  The plans indirectly impacted population growth through initiatives related to family planning and economic development, but not as a direct, targeted measure against Calcutta's population growth specifically.

Statement 2 is correct.  Population growth directly impacts the number of people residing within a given geographical area.  Electoral constituencies are demarcated based on population size to ensure equitable representation.  A rapid increase in Calcutta's population would necessitate readjustments in constituency boundaries and potentially increase the number of representatives.


Statement 3 is incorrect.  Population growth generally leads to an *increase*, not a *decrease*, in the Total Fertility Rate (TFR). A declining TFR is usually indicative of successful family planning programs or socio-economic changes that influence birth rates. While Calcutta might have seen a declining TFR at some point due to such initiatives, directly attributing it solely to population growth is inaccurate.  Population growth itself is not a direct cause of declining TFR; rather, it's often a consequence of high TFRs in the past.


**2. With reference to ecological succession, consider the following statements:**

1.  Phytoplankton are considered pioneer species in primary succession of aquatic ecosystems.
2.  Secondary succession typically begins with a more diverse pioneer community compared to primary succession.
3.  The climax community in a given ecosystem always remains completely stable and unchanging.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct.  In aquatic primary succession,  phytoplankton, being hardy and able to colonize barren environments, are considered pioneer species. They are the first organisms to establish themselves in the newly formed habitat, initiating the process of succession.

Statement 2 is incorrect. Primary succession starts from a completely barren environment, lacking any pre-existing soil or organisms.  Secondary succession, on the other hand, follows a disturbance in an already established ecosystem (e.g., a forest fire).  Therefore, secondary succession usually starts with a more developed environment and a more diverse initial community (compared to the very simple, initial community in primary succession).

Statement 3 is incorrect. While climax communities represent a relatively stable state, they are not completely static.  They are dynamic ecosystems that can be influenced by long-term environmental changes, occasional disturbances, or even the evolutionary changes within the community itself.  The notion of a completely unchanging climax community is an oversimplification of a complex ecological process.


**3. With reference to the concept of sustainable development, consider the following statements:**

1. The Brundtland Commission's definition of sustainable development primarily focuses on intergenerational equity, ensuring that future generations have the same access to resources as the present generation.
2.  The Ramsar philosophy, while not explicitly part of the Brundtland Report, aligns with the broader principles of sustainable development by emphasizing the conservation of wetlands.
3. The Green GDP metric exclusively measures the environmental impact of economic activities, disregarding social and economic factors.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Brundtland Report's definition of sustainable development, "development that meets the needs of the present without compromising the ability of future generations to meet their own needs," is fundamentally about intergenerational equity. It stresses the importance of resource management to ensure fairness and sustainability across generations.


Statement 2 is correct. Although the Ramsar Convention's focus on wetland conservation isn't explicitly detailed within the Brundtland Report, the principles are consistent.  Wetland conservation is crucial for maintaining biodiversity, water resources, and overall environmental health – all key aspects of sustainable development.  The Ramsar philosophy, with its focus on the wise use of wetlands, contributes to the broader goals of sustainable development.


Statement 3 is incorrect.  The Green GDP metric attempts to incorporate environmental costs into the calculation of a nation's economic output.  However, it doesn't *exclusively* focus on environmental aspects; a comprehensive assessment of sustainable development needs to consider social and economic factors as well.  While Green GDP provides a partial view of environmental sustainability, it is not a complete picture of sustainable development.


**4. With reference to environmental change and its impacts, consider the following statements:**

1. Extinction of a species is always a direct and immediate consequence of habitat loss.
2.  The introduction of alien species always results in a trophic cascade impacting the entire ecosystem.
3.  Overexploitation of resources always leads to the immediate extinction of the targeted species.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) None
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While habitat loss is a major driver of extinction, it's not always a direct and immediate cause.  Extinction can be a gradual process, influenced by factors like population size, genetic diversity, and the ability of a species to adapt to changing conditions.  Some species can persist for a time even after significant habitat loss, and extinction may occur later due to compounding factors.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The introduction of alien species can lead to trophic cascades, but it's not always the case. The impact depends on the specific species introduced, the characteristics of the existing ecosystem, and the interactions between the alien species and native organisms. Some alien species may have minimal impact, while others can cause significant disruption.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Overexploitation can lead to population decline and potentially extinction, but it doesn't always result in immediate extinction.  The rate of exploitation, the reproductive capacity of the species, and the existence of conservation efforts all play a role in determining the ultimate outcome.  Some species can recover from periods of overexploitation if given sufficient time and protection.


**5. With reference to in-situ and ex-situ conservation methods, consider the following statements:**

1.  Botanical gardens are exclusively used for ex-situ conservation of plant species.
2.  Biosphere reserves solely employ in-situ conservation methods.
3.  National Parks are exclusively designed for in-situ conservation, with no provision for ex-situ conservation efforts.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) None
(d) 1 and 2 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While botanical gardens are primarily associated with ex-situ conservation, they can also play a supporting role in in-situ conservation efforts through research, propagation, and reintroduction programs.  The conservation strategies employed by botanical gardens are not strictly limited to ex-situ methods.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Biosphere reserves utilize a combination of in-situ and ex-situ conservation approaches. The core zone of a biosphere reserve focuses on in-situ conservation, but buffer and transition zones may incorporate ex-situ components like research facilities or seed banks. The management of biosphere reserves is not restricted to a single conservation method.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  Although National Parks prioritize in-situ conservation, they can also indirectly support ex-situ efforts. For example, research conducted within the park can inform ex-situ breeding programs or contribute to the understanding of species' needs for successful reintroduction.  The management of National Parks is not entirely limited to in-situ conservation strategies.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes a correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Montreal Protocol:**

1.  The Kigali Amendment, signed in 2016, significantly strengthened the Montreal Protocol's regulations on ozone-depleting substances.
2.  The Montreal Protocol's initial focus was solely on phasing out Chlorofluorocarbons (CFCs), with later amendments addressing other ozone-depleting substances.
3.  The Vienna Convention of 1985 established the legal framework for the Montreal Protocol, providing the foundation for international cooperation on ozone layer protection.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Kigali Amendment to the Montreal Protocol, adopted in 2016, significantly expanded the scope of the treaty by phasing down hydrofluorocarbons (HFCs), potent greenhouse gases that contribute to climate change, in addition to ozone-depleting substances.  This demonstrates a crucial interdisciplinary linkage, addressing both ozone depletion and climate change.

Statement 2 is partially incorrect. While CFCs were a primary initial target, the Montreal Protocol was not solely focused on them.  From its inception, it aimed to regulate a broader range of ozone-depleting substances, with the list expanding through subsequent amendments. The Protocol's comprehensive approach is a key element for its success.

Statement 3 is correct. The Vienna Convention for the Protection of the Ozone Layer, signed in 1985, laid the groundwork for the Montreal Protocol.  It established the essential international cooperation and scientific understanding necessary for tackling the complex issue of ozone depletion effectively. The Vienna Convention's framework is essential context for understanding the Montreal Protocol's effectiveness.


**2. With reference to the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs), consider the following statements:**

1.  The Brundtland Commission's definition of sustainable development directly influenced the formulation of the SDGs.
2.  The SDGs aim to achieve a balance between economic growth, environmental protection, and social justice, mirroring the principles outlined in Agenda 21.
3.  The NITI Aayog in India plays a significant role in monitoring and implementing the SDGs within the country.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 2 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Brundtland Commission's report, "Our Common Future," which defined sustainable development as "meeting the needs of the present without compromising the ability of future generations to meet their own needs," fundamentally shaped the global discourse on sustainable development and heavily influenced the formulation of the SDGs. This demonstrates a clear historical and conceptual link.

Statement 2 is correct.  The SDGs, adopted as part of the UN's 2030 Agenda for Sustainable Development, explicitly aim to balance economic progress, environmental sustainability, and social equity.  Agenda 21, adopted at the 1992 Earth Summit, further emphasized these interconnected goals, providing a framework that the SDGs built upon.

Statement 3 is correct. The NITI Aayog (National Institution for Transforming India), a policy think tank of the Government of India, plays a crucial role in coordinating and monitoring the progress of SDG implementation within the country. This highlights the practical application of global policy at the national level.


**3. With reference to the role of the United Nations (UN) in environmental governance, consider the following statements:**

1. The UN established the World Commission on Environment and Development (WCED), also known as the Brundtland Commission, to address global environmental challenges.
2. The UN's Environment Programme (UNEP) is actively involved in promoting the implementation of the Montreal Protocol.
3. The UN's High-level Political Forum on Sustainable Development (HLPF) monitors the implementation of Agenda 21.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The UN played a pivotal role in establishing the WCED (Brundtland Commission) to assess the state of the global environment and propose strategies for sustainable development. This highlights the UN's leadership in setting the global agenda.

Statement 2 is correct. UNEP, a key UN agency, is actively involved in the implementation and monitoring of the Montreal Protocol, providing technical and financial assistance to countries. This underscores the UN's operational capacity in environmental governance.

Statement 3 is correct. The HLPF, a high-level UN body, plays a vital role in reviewing the progress of Agenda 21 and related sustainable development initiatives.  This demonstrates the UN's commitment to long-term monitoring and evaluation of its environmental agenda.


**4. Consider the following statements about the UNFCCC and its related agreements:**

1. The Kyoto Protocol, unlike the UNFCCC, established legally binding emission reduction targets for developed countries.
2. The Paris Agreement, adopted in 2015, superseded the Kyoto Protocol, establishing a new framework for global climate action.
3.  The Copenhagen Accord, while not legally binding, represented a significant step towards a global climate agreement.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The UNFCCC itself sets a framework for international cooperation but does not include specific, legally binding emission reduction targets.  The Kyoto Protocol, however, introduced such targets, particularly for developed nations, based on the principle of "common but differentiated responsibilities."

Statement 2 is correct. The Paris Agreement, adopted in 2015, built upon the UNFCCC and the Kyoto Protocol but established a more comprehensive and inclusive framework for global climate action.  While the Kyoto Protocol focused primarily on developed countries, the Paris Agreement involves all nations in setting nationally determined contributions (NDCs) to reduce greenhouse gas emissions.

Statement 3 is correct. The Copenhagen Accord, though not a legally binding treaty, played a crucial role in advancing the global climate change negotiations. It established important goals, including limiting global temperature increase to below 2°C, and laid the groundwork for the subsequent Paris Agreement.  Its significance lies in its role as a stepping stone towards a more comprehensive agreement.


**5. With reference to  India's environmental legislation, consider the following statements:**

1.  The Environment (Protection) Act, 1986, is considered umbrella legislation, providing a broad framework for environmental protection and encompassing various aspects of pollution control.
2. The Water (Prevention and Control of Pollution) Act, 1974, empowers State Pollution Control Boards (SPCBs) to establish and enforce effluent standards for industries but does not grant them the power to directly close down defaulting plants.
3. The Air (Prevention and Control of Pollution) Act, 1981, initially focused solely on air pollution control, with noise pollution being addressed only through later amendments.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The Environment (Protection) Act, 1986, serves as overarching legislation, setting the stage for broader environmental protection efforts and integrating various pollution control measures.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  The Water (Prevention and Control of Pollution) Act, 1974, as amended in 1988, *does* empower SPCBs to directly close down industrial plants that fail to comply with effluent standards.  This is a significant enforcement tool.

Statement 3 is correct. The Air (Prevention and Control of Pollution) Act, 1981, initially focused primarily on air pollution.  Noise pollution was later included through subsequent amendments, demonstrating the act's evolving scope to address emerging environmental concerns.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple-choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question includes the correct answer and a detailed explanation.


**1. Consider the following statements:**

1. The Millennium Development Goals (MDGs) were superseded by the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs) in 2015, marking a shift in global development priorities.
2. The Faith for Earth Initiative (FEI) is a UN-backed program aimed at achieving the SDGs through faith-based organizations.
3.  The Rio+20 conference played a significant role in the formulation of the SDGs, while the Paris Agreement focused solely on climate change mitigation.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The MDGs, adopted in 2000, were indeed replaced by the SDGs in 2015. The SDGs represent a more comprehensive and interconnected approach to global development, addressing a wider range of social, economic, and environmental challenges.

Statement 2 is incorrect. While the Faith for Earth Initiative (FEI) does aim to achieve the SDGs, it's not a UN-backed program in the sense of being directly funded or administered by the UN.  It operates as an independent initiative leveraging the influence and reach of faith-based organizations to promote sustainable development.

Statement 3 is partially correct.  The Rio+20 conference (UN Conference on Sustainable Development, 2012) was instrumental in setting the stage for the SDGs. The Paris Agreement, while related to sustainable development, focuses primarily on climate change mitigation and adaptation, which is one aspect of the broader SDG agenda.  Therefore, the statement that the Paris agreement focused solely on climate change is a misleading simplification.


**2. With reference to the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs), consider the following statements:**

1. SDG 8, which focuses on decent work and economic growth, is one of the 17 interconnected goals within the broader SDG framework.
2. The UN Agenda 2030, adopted in 2015, explicitly includes the SDGs as a core component of its global development plan.
3. The Partnership for Action on Green Economy (PAGE) actively supports the SDGs by promoting sustainable economic practices, particularly within developing nations.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

All three statements are correct.  Statement 1 accurately identifies SDG 8 as part of the SDG framework. Statement 2 correctly points to the inclusion of SDGs within the UN Agenda 2030.  Statement 3 accurately reflects PAGE's role in supporting the SDGs through its focus on green and inclusive economic growth.  The interconnectedness of these goals is a key feature of the SDG framework, highlighting the need for holistic approaches to global development challenges.


**3. With reference to NITI Aayog, consider the following statements:**

1.  NITI Aayog, established in 2015, replaced the Planning Commission, shifting India's approach from centralized planning to a more cooperative federalist model.
2. The National Action Plan for Sustainable Development, developed by NITI Aayog, outlines India's strategy for achieving the SDGs by 2030, but excludes the involvement of state governments.
3.  NITI Aayog's role includes monitoring India's progress towards the SDGs through initiatives like the Sustainable Development Goals India Index.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. NITI Aayog replaced the Planning Commission, marking a significant shift towards cooperative federalism. The new model emphasizes collaborative policy-making between the central government and state governments.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The National Action Plan for Sustainable Development, while developed primarily by NITI Aayog, actively involves consultations with various stakeholders, including state governments, civil society organizations, and the private sector.  The exclusion of state governments is factually inaccurate.

Statement 3 is correct.  NITI Aayog plays a crucial role in monitoring India's progress on the SDGs, utilizing the SDG India Index and Dashboard as a key tool for tracking performance and identifying areas needing improvement.


**4. Consider the following statements regarding the Human Development Index (HDI):**

1. The HDI, a composite index developed by the UNDP, primarily measures life expectancy, education levels, and per capita income to assess human development.
2.  Amartya Sen's work significantly influenced the conceptual framework of the HDI, though Mahbub ul Haq is solely credited with its creation.
3.  A higher HDI ranking for an Indian state strongly correlates with a higher SDG ranking for that state, indicating a relationship between overall well-being and progress on the SDGs.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 3 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 1, 2, and 3
(d) 2 and 3 only


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The HDI accurately measures life expectancy, education, and per capita income as its core components.

Statement 2 is partially incorrect. While Mahbub ul Haq is largely credited with the HDI's creation, Amartya Sen's work on capabilities and well-being significantly influenced its conceptual underpinnings.  Attributing creation solely to one person is an oversimplification and inaccurate.

Statement 3 is correct.  Empirical data demonstrates a strong positive correlation between HDI and SDG rankings within Indian states. This highlights the interconnectedness of various development aspects.  A higher HDI often reflects better performance across multiple SDG indicators.


**5. Consider the following statements about the SDGs:**

1. The target year for achieving the SDGs is 2030, as outlined in the UN Resolution known as Agenda 2030.
2.  Renewable energy sources are crucial for achieving several SDGs, particularly those related to climate change mitigation and access to clean energy.
3. The SDGs aim to end poverty in all its forms everywhere, but do not explicitly address issues of gender equality or social justice.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 and 2 only
(b) 1 only
(c) 2 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3


**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is correct. The 2030 target year for the SDGs is explicitly stated in the UN's Agenda 2030.

Statement 2 is correct. Renewable energy is essential for progress on multiple SDGs, particularly SDG 7 (Affordable and Clean Energy) and those dealing with climate change (SDG 13).

Statement 3 is incorrect.  The SDGs explicitly address both gender equality (SDG 5) and broader issues of social justice and inclusion within multiple goals.  The statement misrepresents the scope of the SDGs.

Here are some UPSC-style multiple choice questions based on the provided target content, adhering to all specified criteria.  Each question is followed by the correct answer, a detailed explanation, and an analysis of why other options are incorrect.


**1. Consider the following statements regarding the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs):**

1. The DMEO (District Magistrate and Election Officer) solely monitors the implementation of SDGs at the district level.
2. The REDD+ program is entirely unrelated to the achievement of SDGs.
3. The Green Credit Scheme is a government policy directly related to and influenced by the SDGs.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While DMEOs play a role in local governance and development,  monitoring SDG implementation involves multiple governmental and non-governmental organizations at various levels.  It's not solely the responsibility of the DMEO.

Statement 2 is incorrect. REDD+ (Reducing Emissions from Deforestation and forest Degradation) initiatives directly contribute to environmental sustainability, a crucial pillar of the SDGs.  It aims to reduce carbon emissions from deforestation and forest degradation, which is directly related to SDG 13 (Climate Action) and indirectly supports other goals like SDG 15 (Life on Land).

Statement 3 is correct. The Green Credit Scheme, designed to incentivize environmentally friendly practices, is a government policy directly related to the SDGs.  It aligns with several SDGs, particularly those focused on environmental sustainability and economic growth.  The SDGs' framework on environmental and economic sustainability directly influences the design and implementation of such schemes.


**2. With reference to the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs), consider the following statements:**

1. The SDGs were established by the World Health Organization (WHO) in 2015 with a target year of 2030.
2. The UNDP (United Nations Development Programme) plays a significant role in supporting the implementation of SDGs, but it is not the sole implementing agency.
3.  The SDGs aim to balance social, economic, and environmental sustainability, but place the highest priority on economic growth.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) None

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The SDGs were set by the United Nations General Assembly (UNGA), not the WHO, in 2015, with a target year of 2030.  The WHO plays a role in health-related SDGs, but it's not the overarching body responsible for their creation.

Statement 2 is correct. The UNDP is a crucial supporter of SDG implementation, providing technical assistance and resources to countries, but it's not the only actor involved.  Many other UN agencies, governmental bodies, and NGOs contribute to achieving the SDGs.

Statement 3 is incorrect.  While the SDGs aim to balance the three dimensions of sustainability (social, economic, and environmental),  they emphasize the interconnectedness and equal importance of all three, not prioritizing economic growth above the others.  The SDGs recognize that sustainable development requires a holistic approach.


**3. With reference to the Human Development Index (HDI) and its relationship with the Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs), consider the following statements:**

1.  The HDI solely focuses on economic indicators, neglecting social and environmental aspects which are the main focus of SDGs.
2. States with higher HDI scores consistently rank higher in SDG achievement, indicating a strong correlation.
3.  The HDI and SDGs share overlapping components, particularly in education and health, but the HDI is not a perfect predictor of SDG success.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 3 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (d)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. The HDI incorporates social and health indicators (like life expectancy and education levels) alongside economic ones (like GNI per capita). While the SDGs have a broader scope, encompassing environmental sustainability, the HDI does consider social and health factors which are significant components of many SDGs.

Statement 2 is partially correct but an oversimplification.  There's a positive correlation between higher HDI scores and better SDG performance; however,  this relationship is not absolute. Other factors influence SDG achievement, and a high HDI score doesn't guarantee high SDG rankings.

Statement 3 is correct.  The HDI and SDGs share common ground in education and health, which are crucial aspects of both frameworks.  However,  the HDI's focus is narrower than the SDGs', making it an imperfect predictor of success across all 17 goals.  The SDGs encompass a far wider range of social, economic, and environmental goals.


**4.  Consider the following statements about the SDGs' target year and goals:**

1. The SDGs aim to achieve "zero hunger" and "zero AIDS" by 2025.
2. The target year for achieving the SDGs is 2035.
3. The SDGs include goals related to poverty eradication, gender equality, and improved health and well-being.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 3 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect. While "zero hunger" and improved health are SDG goals,  "zero AIDS" is not a specific, standalone SDG goal. The target year for achieving most SDG targets is 2030, not 2025.  The SDGs use a more nuanced approach to tackling diseases like AIDS through various health-related goals.

Statement 2 is incorrect. The target year for achieving the SDGs is 2030, not 2035. This is a crucial detail for understanding the time frame of the global development agenda.

Statement 3 is correct. Poverty eradication, gender equality, and improved health and well-being are core goals of the SDGs.  These are among the 17 main goals, demonstrating the broad scope of the initiative.


**5. With reference to the implementation of SDGs, consider the following statements:**

1.  Only central government agencies are responsible for implementing the SDGs in India.
2. State governments play a significant but limited role in SDG implementation, primarily focusing on local issues.
3.  Local governments and communities are crucial partners in implementing the SDGs, contributing to ground-level action.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 3 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2, and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 1 is incorrect.  SDG implementation in India is a multi-level effort. While the central government sets national targets and policies, state and local governments play critical roles in adapting and implementing these goals according to their specific contexts.

Statement 2 is incorrect. State governments have a substantial role in SDG implementation.  They are responsible for many programs and policies directly related to SDG targets.  Their involvement extends beyond local issues, encompassing broader state-level strategies.

Statement 3 is correct. Local governments and community participation are essential for effective SDG implementation.  Local knowledge, context-specific strategies, and community engagement are crucial for achieving the goals on the ground.  The success of the SDGs depends heavily on the active participation of local actors.

**1. Consider the following statements regarding biomes:**

1.  A biome's primary characteristic is its unique set of flora and fauna, irrespective of climatic conditions.
2.  The tropical rainforest biome, while known for its high biodiversity, exhibits relatively low levels of precipitation compared to other biomes.
3.  Biomes are large-scale ecosystems classified primarily based on their climatic conditions, influencing vegetation and animal life.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 3 accurately reflects the defining characteristics of biomes.  Biomes are indeed large-scale ecosystems categorized primarily by their climate, which dictates the types of plants (vegetation) and animals (fauna) that can thrive within them.  Climate influences factors like temperature, precipitation, and sunlight, all of which shape the overall ecosystem.  

Statement 1 is incorrect because while flora and fauna are key components of a biome, climate is the dominant factor in defining its type and characteristics.  A biome's plant and animal life are *consequences* of its climate, not the primary defining feature.  Different biomes can have similar plant or animal species, but their climates will differ significantly.

Statement 2 is false. The tropical rainforest biome is characterized by extremely high levels of precipitation, contributing to its lush vegetation and high biodiversity.  This high rainfall is essential for supporting the dense vegetation and the diverse array of plant and animal life found in these regions.  A low precipitation rate would define a different biome altogether, such as a desert.


**2. With reference to ecosystems, consider the following statements:**

1.  Decomposers, while crucial for nutrient cycling, play a minimal role in the overall energy flow within an ecosystem.
2.  The most stable ecosystems are characterized by low biodiversity and minimal interaction with the physical environment.
3.  Producers form the base of the food web, providing energy to all other trophic levels within the ecosystem.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 3 only
(d) 1 and 2 only

**Correct Answer:** (c)

**Explanation:**

Statement 3 correctly identifies the fundamental role of producers in an ecosystem. Producers, primarily plants and algae, are autotrophs that convert sunlight into energy through photosynthesis. This energy forms the base of the food web, supporting all other trophic levels (primary consumers, secondary consumers, etc.).  Without producers, the entire ecosystem's energy flow would collapse.

Statement 1 is incorrect. Decomposers, such as bacteria and fungi, are essential for nutrient cycling. They break down dead organic matter, releasing nutrients back into the environment, making them available for producers.  This nutrient cycling is a vital part of the ecosystem's energy flow, as nutrients are essential for plant growth and the entire food chain.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  Ecosystem stability is directly related to biodiversity and the system's ability to withstand disturbances. High biodiversity generally equates to greater resilience.  A diverse ecosystem has multiple species playing similar roles, so if one species is affected, others can compensate.  Interaction with the physical environment is also crucial; ecosystems adapt and evolve in response to environmental changes.  Low biodiversity and isolation make an ecosystem vulnerable to collapse.


**3. With reference to anthropogenic biomes, consider the following statements:**

1.  Anthropogenic biomes are exclusively composed of human-introduced species, devoid of any naturally occurring organisms.
2.  Croplands, while significantly altered by human activities, retain many characteristics of their original natural biome.
3.  Anthropogenic biomes represent a significant departure from natural biomes, reflecting the extensive impact of human activities on the environment.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 3 accurately describes the defining characteristic of anthropogenic biomes. These biomes are fundamentally altered by human activities, resulting in ecosystems that differ significantly from their natural counterparts. Human intervention, such as agriculture, urbanization, and resource extraction, fundamentally changes the landscape, species composition, and ecological processes.

Statement 1 is incorrect.  Anthropogenic biomes are not entirely devoid of naturally occurring organisms. While human activities dramatically alter these environments, many native species may persist, albeit in altered numbers and distributions. The interaction between introduced and native species is a complex aspect of anthropogenic biomes.

Statement 2 is partially true but ultimately misleading. Croplands are heavily modified ecosystems, but they might retain some remnants of the original vegetation or soil characteristics. However, the dominant feature is the human-driven cultivation of crops, making it a fundamentally different ecosystem from its natural predecessor. The presence of some original features doesn't negate the significant alteration caused by human intervention.


**4. Consider the following statements about greenwashing:**

1.  Greenwashing is a form of deceptive marketing primarily used by small businesses to enhance their image.
2.  Vague or unsubstantiated claims, such as "eco-friendly," are a common tactic employed in greenwashing.
3.  Greenwashing only involves visual representations, such as images of nature, to create a false impression of sustainability.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 2 only
(b) 1 and 2 only
(c) 2 and 3 only
(d) 1, 2 and 3

**Correct Answer:** (a)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 accurately describes a key element of greenwashing. Businesses often use vague and unsubstantiated claims to create a false sense of environmental responsibility.  Terms like "eco-friendly" or "sustainable" are frequently used without clear evidence or certification to support these claims, misleading consumers.

Statement 1 is incorrect. Greenwashing is not limited to small businesses; it's a widespread practice across various industries and business sizes, from small startups to large multinational corporations. The motivation is to enhance their brand image and attract environmentally conscious consumers.

Statement 3 is incorrect. Greenwashing isn't solely reliant on visual representations. While images of nature are a common tactic, it encompasses a broader range of deceptive marketing strategies.  This includes making misleading comparisons to less sustainable alternatives, hiding negative environmental impacts, and using misleading certifications or labels.  The goal is to create a perception of environmental responsibility without substantial changes in practices.


**5. With reference to ecological organization, consider the following statements:**

1.  The hierarchical order of ecological units is: Landscape - Ecosystem - Community - Population.
2.  An ecotone is a sharp boundary between two distinct ecosystems, devoid of species from either ecosystem.
3.  A community represents a collection of populations of different species interacting within a specific habitat.


Which of the statements given above is/are correct?
(a) 1 only
(b) 3 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) 2 and 3 only

**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 3 correctly defines a biological community.  A community is an assemblage of populations of various species interacting within a defined area or habitat. These interactions can include competition, predation, symbiosis, and other ecological relationships.

Statement 1 is incorrect. The correct hierarchical order is: Population - Community - Ecosystem - Landscape.  A population is a group of individuals of the same species; several interacting populations form a community; communities and their physical environment comprise an ecosystem; and a mosaic of interconnected ecosystems forms a landscape.

Statement 2 is incorrect.  An ecotone is a transition zone between two distinct ecosystems.  It’s characterized by a mixture of species from both adjacent ecosystems, often exhibiting higher biodiversity than either of the individual ecosystems due to the edge effect.  The boundary isn't sharp; it's a gradual change in environmental conditions and species composition.

**1. Consider the following statements about ecosystem characteristics:**

1.  An ecotone is a sharp boundary between two distinct ecosystems, characterized by a sudden shift in species composition.
2.  Ecoclines represent gradual transitions between ecosystems, showing a continuous change in environmental factors and species distribution.
3.  Edge effects are always negative, reducing biodiversity at the boundaries of ecosystems.

Which of the statements given above is/are correct?

(a) 1 only
(b) 2 only
(c) 1 and 2 only
(d) None


**Correct Answer:** (b)

**Explanation:**

Statement 2 accurately describes ecoclines.  Ecoclines are indeed gradual transitions between ecosystems, exhibiting a continuous change in environmental factors (like temperature, humidity, salinity) and a corresponding shift in species composition. This gradual change contrasts with the sharp boundaries often associated with ecotones.

Statement 1 is incorrect because ecotones are *not* always sharp boundaries.
